14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"Jordan has accused the king's half-brother of plotting to destabilize the country, following a string of arrests","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/jordan-foiled-a-plot-arresting-16-including-kings-half-brother-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6069ccfba7d803001963ea8b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FILE PHOTO - King of Jordan Abdullah II addresses the European Parliament in Strasbourg, France January 15, 2020. REUTERS/Vincent Kessler\" height=\"2060\" width=\"4120\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>King of Jordan Abdullah II addresses the European Parliament in Strasbourg.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Deputy prime minister Ayman Safadi said the government has foiled a plot, following several arrests.</li>\n<li>Prince Hamza, the Jordanian king&#39;s half-brother, said he is under house arrest.</li>\n<li>Allies, including Saudi Arabia and the US, expressed support for the king.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The deputy prime minister of Jordan, Ayman Safadi, has said that a plot to destabilize the country has been foiled.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-04-03/jordan-arrests-royal-family-member-others-on-security-concerns\">According to Bloomberg</a>, the plot allegedly involved King Abdullah II&#39;s half-brother, former Crown Prince Hamza Bin Hussein, Safadi said at a news conference in Amman, the nation&#39;s capital, on Sunday.</p><p>Safadi also said more than 16 people were arrested, including Prince Hamza, who was placed under house arrest on Saturday.</p><p>&#34;There was an effort to target Jordan&#39;s security and stability, this effort was foiled,&#34; Safadi said, but gave no evidence to back up the claims.</p><p>Jordan, a US ally, often acts as a force for moderation in the turbulent region, making its stability essential. In August, the US provided the kingdom with <a href=\"https://www.jordantimes.com/news/local/jordan-receives-around-700-million-us-grant\">$700 million in aid</a>.</p><p>On Saturday, chairman of the joint chiefs of staff, Major General Yousef Huneiti, denied reports that Prince Hamza had been arrested. He added that he had been ordered to &#34;stop activities that are being exploited to target Jordan&#39;s security and stability.&#34;</p><p>Prince Hamza has denied the allegations, telling the BBC he was &#34;not part of any conspiracy,&#34; in a <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-56626370\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"Link to video\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">video</a> provided by his lawyer.</p><p>&#34;There is no conspiracy here. Whatever concoction they&#39;re attempting to create or whatever narrative that they&#39;re attempting to sell, the basic fact is that this is all about human dignity here, freedom from arbitrary government, freedom from invasive security apparatuses and services...&#34; he said in the video.</p><p>In 2004, King Abdullah II dismissed Prince Hamza as heir, opting for his eldest son, Hussein, and consolidating his power.</p><p>Saudi Arabia, the United Arab Emirates, Qatar, Egypt and other Arab states expressed support for King Abdullah, Bloomberg reported.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Noor Al Hussein  (@QueenNoor) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1378639005164707840?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 4, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>The US has also vocalized support. State Department spokesman Ned Price said: &#34;We are closely following the reports and in touch with Jordanian officials. King Abdullah is a key partner of the United States, and he has our full support.&#34;</p><p>Prince Hamza&#39;s mother, Queen Noor al Hussein, has expressed support for her son, calling the allegations &#34;wicked slander.&#34;</p><p> </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4d884560bf1f00280799b6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"New Jersey Governor Phil Murphy\" height=\"1600\" width=\"2400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>New Jersey Governor Phil Murphy\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jose F. Moreno/The Philadelphia Inquirer/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>New Jersey Gov. Phil Murphy sent a letter to Hollywood studios like Netflix and Disney on Thursday.</li>\n<li>Murphy wanted to lure studios to the state after backlash to Georgia&#39;s new voting law.</li>\n<li>Some media companies like ViacomCBS and AT&#38;T have issued statements opposing the controversial bill.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>New Jersey wants to be in business with Hollywood.</p><p>The state&#39;s governor, Phil Murphy, sent a letter to major Hollywood studios like Disney, Warner Bros., and Netflix on Thursday in an attempt to lure business away from Georgia after it passed a controversial voting law, according to several outlets that obtained the letter, including <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/new-jersey-tries-to-woo-film-studios-from-georgia-amid-voting-law-blowback-11617314734\">The Wall Street Journal</a> and <a href=\"https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/new-jersey-attempts-to-poach-georgias-film-business-amid-backlash-to-states-new-voting-law\">The Hollywood Reporter.</a></p><p>Gov. Brian Kemp, a Republican, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-lawmakers-pass-sweeping-election-administration-bill-2021-3\">signed the sweeping elections bill</a> into law on March 25, which has been met with backlash from Democrats and civil-rights groups who say it targets Black communities. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-new-election-law-means-for-voters-and-officials-explainer-2021-3\">Among the most controversial aspects</a> of the bill are changes to absentee voting and banning volunteers from delivering food, water, and other items to people waiting in long voting lines.</p><p>Murphy wrote that &#34;restricting the right to vote is more than just wrong, it&#39;s un-American&#34; and that the &#34;vast majority&#34; see the law as &#34;an attack on people of color by a Governor and Legislature willing to do anything to stay in power.&#34;</p><p>Georgia offers attractive tax incentives that have made it a major Hollywood production hub. Murphy emphasized New Jersey&#39;s 30% tax credit on film projects and a 40% subsidy for any brick-and-mortar studio development, according to THR.</p><p>&#34;Our new $14.5 billion economic incentive package makes the Garden State just as competitive as Georgia to attract film and television production businesses,&#34; Murphy wrote. &#34;One thing is clear: when it comes to social policies, corporate responsibility, and - not to be overlooked - economic opportunity, New Jersey is now a top contender for your business.&#34;</p><p><a href=\"https://deadline.com/2021/04/viacomcbs-georgia-voting-bill-comcast-1234726035/\">Some media companies have issued statements</a> condemning the Georgia law, but have not called for a boycott of the state.</p><p>ViacomCBS, the parent company of Paramount Pictures, was the first major media company to speak out: &#34;We unequivocally believe in the importance of all Americans having an equal right to vote and oppose the recent Georgia voting rights law or any effort that impedes the ability to exercise this vital constitutional right.&#34;</p><p>Comcast, NBCUniversal&#39;s corporate parent, and AT&#38;T, which owns WarnerMedia, Warner Bros., and Atlanta-based CNN, followed with their own statements.</p><p>Comcast said: &#34;Voting is fundamental to our democracy. We believe that all Americans should enjoy equitable access to secure elections and we have long supported and promoted voter education, registration and participation campaigns across the country to achieve that goal. Efforts to limit or impede access to this vital constitutional right for any citizen are not consistent with our values.&#34;</p><p>AT&#38;T&#39;s CEO John Stankey said in part: &#34;We believe the right to vote is sacred and we support voting laws that make it easier for more Americans to vote in free, fair and secure elections. We understand that election laws are complicated, not our company&#39;s expertise and ultimately the responsibility of elected officials. But, as a company, we have a responsibility to engage.&#34;</p><p>Disney and Netflix have not released statements regarding the Georgia voting law.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original after leaving en masse amid <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-killed-new-york-city-big-apple-will-be-back-2020-12\">the COVID-19 pandemic that hit the city hard</a>. </p><p>For the first time since the beginning of 2020, the number of sales topped the year-ago total, according to a <a href=\"https://www.millersamuel.com/regions/manhattan/\">report by Douglas Elliman Real Estate brokerage</a> that was first covered by <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-04-02/manhattan-homebuyers-are-back-but-they-re-here-for-the-deals?srnd=premium\">Bloomberg</a>.</p><p>Apartment sales in the borough increased 2.1% in the first three months this year as compared to the same time last year when the pandemic struck the city, the report said. </p><p>The rebound in March alone was the strongest since 2007, as about 1,500 homes in Manhattan were under contract for sale, according to a report from <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/manhattan-residential-sales-in-march-soared-to-highest-level-in-14-years-11617361200?mod=pls_whats_news_us_business_f\">The Wall Street Journal</a> that cited real-estate analytics firm UrbanDigs. </p><p>Buyers are taking advantage of the lower prices, too, with most of those sales closing at or below the asking price. Eager homebuyers are propelling a real-estate surge as Manhattan lags far behind.</a></em></p><p>The west and east side of Manhattan, as well as downtown, had the strongest sales compared with last year, as upper Manhattan and Midtown had fewer deals, the WSJ said. </p><p>Six months into the pandemic, <a the new normal for the city, even if it wasn&#39;t as drastic as during 2020. </p><p>With businesses allowing employees to work from home during the pandemic, many people were able to move to outer boroughs for more space and lower prices. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/brooklyn-real-estate-demand-prices-statistics-coronavirus-recovery-2021-1\">Brooklyn proved resilient</a> amid the pandemic, as its sales began bouncing back in the last three months of 2020.  </p><p>Many others during the pandemic <a system'","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/animation-saturn-rings-orbit-spin-faster-than-speed-of-sound-2021-3","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/605e06758e71b30018519019?format=jpeg\" alt=\"saturn rings radio\" height=\"1440\" width=\"1920\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Saturn&#39;s rings, imaged based on radio data from NASA&#39;s Cassini spacecraft. Green indicates regions with particles smaller than 5 centimeters; purple is where no particles are that small. The white area is so dense that it blocked radio signals.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://photojournal.jpl.nasa.gov/catalog/PIA07873\" target=\"_blank\">NASA/JPL</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/photos-jupiter-saturn-align-conjunction-2020-12\">Saturn&#39;s</a> seven icy <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/saturn-hubble-photo-reveals-summer-winter-storms-2020-7\">rings</a> each spin at their own speed, behaving like a &#34;mini solar system.&#34;</li>\n<li>Planetary scientist James O&#39;Donoghue made a beautifully simple <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/animation-explains-mars-communication-delay-nasa-astronauts-2020-9\">animation</a> to show how it works.</li>\n<li>But the rings are temporary: Saturn is slowly swallowing them, according to O&#39;Donoghue&#39;s research.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>If star-hopping aliens ever visited our solar system, Saturn is probably the planet they&#39;d remember.</p><p>The seven giant rings circling its equator make Saturn the most distinct planet orbiting the sun. It may not be obvious in images of the hula-hoop planet, but the ice and rock chunks that make up those rings are circling Saturn at rates nearly 70 times the speed of sound. What&#39;s more, each ring is moving at its own pace.</p><p>&#34;In a way, the ring system is like a mini solar system,&#34; <a href=\"https://twitter.com/physicsJ\">James O&#39;Donoghue</a>, a planetary scientist at Japan&#39;s space agency, JAXA, told Insider. &#34;Objects close to Saturn orbit faster otherwise they would fall in, while objects far away can afford to go slower. This is the same for planets.&#34;</p><p>In his free time, <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCSaCQr2ppyNUY_kjnWY1yVQ\">O&#39;Donoghue makes animations</a> about physics and the solar system. Some of his others have demonstrated that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/former-nasa-scientist-video-shows-moon-has-no-dark-side-2019-11\">there&#39;s no &#34;dark side&#34; of the moon</a>, the true <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/animation-reveals-invisible-center-of-solar-system-not-sun-2020-7\">center of the solar system isn&#39;t the sun</a>, and Earth has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scientists-animation-reveals-earth-has-2-types-of-day-2020-9\">two types of day</a>.</p><p>When he put his skills to work to depict Saturn&#39;s rings, O&#39;Donoghue created an animation (below) that shows how the each ring moves through its own motions in a beautiful, circular dance.</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/u3rpAHKVh84\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe><p>In the animation, the line labeled &#34;synchronous orbit&#34; is synced up with the spin of Saturn itself, so it shows which parts of the rings you would see over time if you stood at that spot on the planet.</p><p>Saturn&#39;s slowest, outermost ring spins at about 37,000 mph (16.4 kilometers per second) - slower than the rotation of Saturn itself. The innermost chunks of ice and rock shoot through space at about 52,000 mph (23.2 kilometers per second).</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/605e021c106eb50019d05d1a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"saturn rings illustration\" height=\"1440\" width=\"1920\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An illustration of Saturn&#39;s rings up close.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://images.nasa.gov/details-0400741\" target=\"_blank\">NASA</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Up close, Saturn&#39;s rings aren&#39;t as chaotic as their speeds might make them seem. According to O&#39;Donoghue, grains of ice on neighboring tracks are only moving at a few centimeters per minute relative to each other.</p><p>&#34;That speed is like walking one step every 30 minutes, or similar to rush hour traffic,&#34; he <a href=\"https://twitter.com/physicsJ/status/1272133243165270023\">said</a> on Twitter. &#34;So collisions aren&#39;t very dramatic.&#34;</p><h2>Saturn is slowly swallowing its rings</h2><p>In addition to being incredibly fast-moving, Saturn&#39;s rings are very long and thin. If you unfurled them - as O&#39;Donoghue did in the image below - all the planets would fit comfortably within their length.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/605e01266746fb0018a73eb8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"saturn rings solar system o&#39;donoghue\" height=\"2048\" width=\"4096\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">James O&#39;Donoghue</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>But in total, the rings have just 1/5,000th the mass of our moon.</p><p>&#34;In other words, our moon could be used to make 5,000 Saturn ring systems,&#34; O&#39;Donoghue told Insider. &#34;This highlights how extremely thin and fragile the rings of Saturn are.&#34;</p><p>This fragility is a subject of O&#39;Donoghue&#39;s scientific research. In studying Saturn&#39;s upper atmosphere, he and his colleagues <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/press-release/goddard/2018/ring-rain\">found</a> that the rings are slowly disappearing. Thousands of kilograms of ring material rain onto the planet every second. At that rate, the rings shouldn&#39;t last more than 300 million years in their current &#34;full&#34; form, he said.</p><p>&#34;Saturn&#39;s ring system is not exactly stable, appearing to be more like a temporary debris field of some ancient moon or comet which got too close and broke apart, rather than a permanent feature,&#34; O&#39;Donoghue added. &#34;We can count ourselves lucky we live in a time when Saturn&#39;s rings have such an enormous presence in the solar system.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a acceleration out of recession, led by projections for earnings in the energy sector to more than double.</p><p>A big wave of financial reports should hit Wall Street in mid-April, with big banks including <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/jpm-stock\">JPMorgan Chase</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/gs-stock\">Goldman Sachs</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/wfc-stock\">Wells Fargo</a> among the companies that will kick off the first-quarter earnings season for 2021.</p><p>Ahead of that, Wall Street companies overall to post a 6% increase in bottom-up per-share earnings, according to FactSet. A 6% rise would represent the largest increase since the financial-data firm began tracking the earnings estimate in the second quarter of 2002. Earnings, on average, are currently expected to come in at $39.86 per share.</p><p>The bottom-up EPS estimate is an aggregation of the median first-quarter earnings-per-share estimates for all of the companies in the S&#38;P 500, FactSet said in a note published Thursday.</p><p>The projected 6% increase stands out in part because a bottom-up EPS estimate usually decreases during a quarter. FactSet said during the past five years, the estimate has recorded a decline of 4.2% during a quarter, and during the past 15 years, it has tended to post a decrease of 5.1%.</p><p>Analysts &#34;may have been too aggressive in their downward revisions to EPS estimates during the first half of 2020 at the height of the COVID-19 lockdowns,&#34; wrote John Butters, senior earnings analyst at FactSet, in looking at the factors behind the boost in first-quarter projections.</p><p>The global economy sunk into recession last year as the coronavirus pandemic forced businesses worldwide to close or reduce operations to curb the spread of the respiratory disease. The US economy contracted by 33% in the second quarter of 2020.</p><p>But analysts in the third quarter of 2020 began raising their earnings expectations for that quarter and beyond. FactSet foresees US gross domestic product expanding by 5.7% in 2021, higher than the projected 4% rate on December 31.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-with-best-profitability-growth-estimates-gs-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Goldman Sachs says buy these 33 stocks now as profits rebound for companies that suffered the most during the pandemic</a></em></p><p>Rising commodity prices and interest rates also appear to be fueling upward revisions. Oil prices have jumped by more than 20% to top $59 a barrel during the first quarter and the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/rates/u-s--rates-10-years\">yield on the 10-year Treasury note</a> quickly scaled up above 1.7% during the first three months of this year from 0.92%. </p><p>The highest percentage increases in bottom-up EPS estimates are for the energy, materials, and financials sectors as they are &#34;likely benefitting from either higher commodity prices (Energy and Materials) or higher interest rates (Financials),&#34; said Butters.</p><p>Per-share earnings estimates for the energy sector have shot up by 123%, to $2.55 from $1.14, the largest boost in projections among the 11 sectors tracked on the S&#38;P 500 index. The financial sector is forecast to post a collective earnings increase of about 13% for the first quarter.</p><p>&#34;Finally, companies in the S&#38;P 500 have been much more optimistic in their EPS guidance than normal,&#34; said Butters, noting that 61 companies have issued positive first-quarter guidance, well above the five-year average of 35.</p><p>&#34;If 61 is the final number for the quarter, it will mark the highest number of S&#38;P 500 companies issuing positive EPS guidance for a quarter since FactSet began tracking this metric in 2006,&#34; he said.</p><div src=\"https://i.insider.com/6069f6db856cd700198a3148?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Houston\" height=\"2995\" width=\"4500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>People drive on Interstate 45 toward downtown Houston.\n<p class=\"copyright\">BRENDAN SMIALOWSKI/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Department of Transportation has paused a Houston-area highway widening project.</li>\n<li>In the past, highways were constructed with no regard for minority communities.</li>\n<li>The Biden administration is seeking to address past racial inequities in planning decisions.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The US Department of Transportation is using a provision of the Civil Rights Act of 1964 to pause construction on a highway widening project near Houston, an uncommon move that could be an early test of President Joe Biden&#39;s commitment to addressing past racial inequities, <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2021/04/01/dot-texas-highway-equity-478864\">according to Politico</a>.</p><p>As the populous region continues to grow, the Interstate 45 highway project has been heralded as a way to reduce congestion and improve commute times, but the additional lanes would also impact several heavily Black and Latino neighborhoods, forcing residents, businesses, and houses of worship in the path to relocate.</p><p>The construction plan, known as the North Houston Highway Improvement Project, would widen the highway into three segments.</p><p>Local resistance to the I-45 project had been brewing for years, with many <a href=\"https://kinder.rice.edu/urbanedge/2019/06/17/houston-i-45-project-txdot-independence-heights\">hearkening back</a> to the 1950s when freeway routes were <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/cities/2018/feb/21/roads-nowhere-infrastructure-american-inequality\">deliberately drawn</a> to impact Black communities and divide people by race and class.</p><p>The I-45 project has at least been temporarily halted, with Transportation secretary Pete Buttigieg now at the helm of the sprawling federal department.</p><p>Federal transportation authorities in March <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/f/?id=00000178-8f27-d59d-a7f9-bf6fa4bb0000\">sent a letter</a> asking Texas to pause contracts on the widening project while they reviewed racial justice complaints covered by <a href=\"https://www.fhwa.dot.gov/civilrights/programs/title_vi/#:~:text=Title%20VI%20of%20the%20Civil%20Rights%20Act%20of%201964%2C%20prohibits,%2C%20color%2C%20and%20national%20origin.\">Title VI of the Civil Rights Act</a>, along with environmental concerns.</p><p>The provision states that &#34;no person in the United States shall, on the ground of race, color, or national origin, be excluded from participation in, be denied the benefits of, or be subjected to discrimination under any program or activity receiving Federal financial assistance.&#34;</p><p><strong><em>Read more: </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/issues-that-could-tank-bidens-infrastructure-plan-congress-salt-taxes-2021-4\"><em>Here are 9 hurdles Biden&#39;s infrastructure plan would have to overcome in Congress before it can become law</em></a></p><p>In a letter written to the Texas Department of Transportation, the Federal Highway Administration cited community opposition in reviewing the I-45 widening project, mentioning Houston-area Democratic Congresswoman Sheila Jackson Lee, Air Alliance Houston, and the community organization Texas Housers.</p><p>&#34;I think [Buttigieg] was engaged, interested and fair,&#34; Jackson Lee told Politico after speaking with the secretary. &#34;I think he was chagrined at federal dollars being used with such disregard of community views.&#34;</p><p>The congresswoman feels that the Texas Department of Transportation &#34;blatantly violated&#34; the Title VI provision.</p><p>The project&#39;s pause, which is being driven by civil rights laws, has thrilled grassroots activists and Washington figures.</p><p>Fred Wagner, an attorney and former chief counsel at the Federal Highway Administration under the Obama administration, told Politico that taking such a step was a big change.</p><p>&#34;It just doesn&#39;t happen very often,&#34; he said. &#34;For DOT to step in, potentially, and say &#39;We don&#39;t think it&#39;s an appropriate solution,&#39; would be a really huge deal.&#34;</p><p>Buttigieg, who is seeking to reimagine the country&#39;s transportation system, also hopes <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2021/03/08/biden-buttigieg-acial-equity-473928\">to dismantle</a> old processes that disenfranchised Americans of color from past planning conversations, especially when entire neighborhoods were destroyed by urban planners when the modern US highway network was first built in the 20th Century.</p><p>&#34;This is not just a matter of halfway accidental neglect,&#34; he said <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2021/03/08/biden-buttigieg-acial-equity-473928\">in a Politico interview</a> last month. &#34;We&#39;re talking about some really intentional decisions that happened, and a lot of them happened with federal dollars.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/6064dd016183e100198199b0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"AP21084746357769\" height=\"2872\" width=\"3829\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Downtown Burlington High School.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Charles Krupa</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Students at the school spent the previous six months learning remotely after toxic chemicals that can have dangerous health effects, called <a href=\"https://www.epa.gov/pcbs/learn-about-polychlorinated-biphenyls-pcbs#healtheffects\">PCBs</a>, were found in the school building.&#160;</p>\n\tThe district signed a department store. Dividers separate the huge space into dozens of classrooms, plus a <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/macys-converted-into-high-school-vermont-79ab42cb178f6a26e5239d6688caed8d\">cafeteria, library, and physical education room.</a></p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-biggest-potential-retail-acquisition-targets-for-2021-2020-12\">9 retail brands that are prime M&#38;A targets in 2021, according to experts</a><strong><br /></strong></em></p>\n\tThe escalators are one of the features that make Downtown Burlington High School different from others. reading books where they once sold fine China; taking phone calls in converted changing rooms; and learning science in the old suit racks,\" he continued.</p>\n\tThe china department was transformed into a library, and shelves that once held dinnerware now hold books for high school students.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6064ddf3daf0f10018f99544?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Downtown Burlington High School\" height=\"2242\" width=\"2989\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Downtown Burlington High School.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Charles Krupa</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The gym, located in the warehouse, is still a work in progress.</p>\n\tShuttered American malls are a symptom of the retail apocalypse that led to 9,300 store closings in 2019, 8,300 in 2020, and already more than 1,000 in 2021.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6064de00daf0f10018f99545?format=jpeg\" alt=\"AP21084746481358 (1)\" height=\"2680\" width=\"3574\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Downtown Burlington High School.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Charles Krupa</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>This trend is especially deadly for malls, which rely on anchor stores like Macy's and Sears to drive foot traffic inside.&#160;</p>\n\tAs malls close, some simply sit empty and abandoned. House inquiry says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-aide-pushed-for-connections-get-covid-19-contracts-report-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6069a8dda7d803001963ea6a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Peter Navarro\" height=\"3822\" width=\"5096\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>White House Trade and Manufacturing Policy Director Peter Navarro speaks during a briefing on the coronavirus pandemic in the press briefing room of the White House on March 27, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Drew Angerer/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Peter Navarro, Trump&#39;s former trade adviser, is accused of rewarding companies with White House links.</li>\n<li>Trump officials steered contracts to companies without &#34;adequate diligence,&#34; a House inquiry says.</li>\n<li>On one occasion, Navarro pushed for a brand-new start-up to secure a $354 million contract.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A senior adviser to former President Donald Trump pushed agency officials to secure huge COVID-19 contracts for politically connected and untested firms, according to documents from an <a href=\"https://www.documentcloud.org/documents/20534011-2021-03-30select-sub-to-mayorkas-fenton-re-dhs-fema\">inquiry by the Select Subcommittee on the Coronavirus Crisis.</a></p><p>Peter Navarro, who served as a trade adviser to Trump, is one of the officials accused of pursuing a &#34;haphazard and ineffective approach to procurement&#34; and steering contracts &#34;to particular companies without adequate diligence or competitions.&#34;</p><p>There are numerous examples outlined in the inquiry of how the Trump aide played a significant role in rewarding multimillion-dollar deals to companies with connections to the White House, <a href=\"https://www.propublica.org/article/trump-covid-pandemic-contracts?utm_source=twitter&utm_medium=socialcial\">ProPublica</a> reported.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/heres-who-got-hired-in-washington-this-week-kayleigh-mcenany-2021-4\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Washington moves of the week: A top Trump White House staffer lands a TV gig and a former Kamala Harris aide heads to a lobbying firm</a></em></p><p>On one occasion, Navarro awarded a $96 million deal for respirators to a company with links to the administration - Airboss Defense Group (ADG).</p><p>Retired Army general Jack Keane, a Trump ally and paid consultant for ADG, sent a catalog of the company&#39;s items to Navarro on March 22, 2020. Keane had just been awarded the Presidential Medal of Freedom by Trump days earlier.</p><p>Navarro and members of the White House Coronavirus Task Force had a phone call with representatives from ADG later that day, according to the House inquiry.</p><p>Then, a day after the call, ADG submitted a $96.4 million proposal to Navarro&#39;s team. He responded by telling the firm in an email that they could &#34;consider it done,&#34; the documents show.</p><p>Federal Emergency Management Agency officials were quickly sent an invoice and pressured into signing the contract, ProPublica said.</p><p>On another occasion, the Trump aide pushed for an untested pharmaceutical company to sign a major deal to produce pharmaceutical ingredients and generic drugs. </p><p>The $354 million contract went to a newly-formed start-up, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-trump-admin-gives-812m-contract-to-small-virginia-firm-2020-5\">Phlow.</a> &#34;It was the largest contract ever awarded by BARDA (Biomedical Advanced Research and Development Authority), even though Phlow was a first-time government contractor that had incorporated just months earlier in January 2020,&#34; documents from the Select Subcommittee show.</p><p>Navarro had been introduced to Phlow&#39;s chief executive months earlier, the documents say. He had also developed a friendship with a Phlow board member over their shared China skepticism, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-trump-admin-gives-812m-contract-to-small-virginia-firm-2020-5\">Insider&#39;s Tom Porter</a> reported.</p><p>The Trump aide also put pressure on agency officials to get the deal done quickly, the inquiry finds. &#34;My head is going to explode if this contract does not get immediately approved,&#34; Navarro wrote to BARDA officials.</p><p>The former trade adviser is accused of coordinating with executives at the Eastman Kodak Company. The photography business has a &#34;complete lack of experience in the field,&#34; the subcommittee&#39;s letter says. Nevertheless, the firm entered into a letter of intent in June 2020 to manufacture pharmaceutical agents.</p><p>Navarro has made <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peter-navarro-trump-advisor-calls-fauci-father-of-coronavirus-fox-news-rant-2021-3\">headlines</a> in recent days for spreading baseless claims about COVID-19 and for railing against Dr. Anthony Fauci.</p><p>During a Fox News interview with Rachel Campos-Duffy, Navarro referred to Fauci as &#34;the father of the actual virus.&#34; He also called Fauci a &#34;sociopath and a liar&#34; who had &#34;nothing to do with the vaccine,&#34; Insider&#39;s SinÃ©ad Baker reported.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-bidens-2-trillion-infrastructure-plan-means-for-you-2021-4\">$2 trillion infrastructure plan</a>, making the case that the legislation would be transformational for the country.</p><p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/MeetThePress/status/1378690503865171969\">During an interview</a> on NBC&#39;s &#34;Meet the Press,&#34; Buttigieg said the American Jobs Plan represented &#34;a generational investment&#34; that would produce &#34;economic growth that&#39;s going to go on for years and years.&#34;</p><p>&#34;Infrastructure is the foundation that makes it possible for Americans to thrive,&#34; he said. &#34;And what we know is that foundation has been crumbling.</p><p>Buttigieg made the argument that the current transportation network, built up decades ago, has to meet the needs of a modern society.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;re still coasting on infrastructure choices that were made in the 1950s,&#34; he said. &#34;Now&#39;s our chance to make infrastructure choices for the future that are going to serve us well in the 2030s and onto the middle of the century when we will be judged for whether we meet this moment here in the 2020s.&#34;</p><p>Biden&#39;s massive plan includes $621 billion in transportation infrastructure investments, with direct funding for road and bridge repairs, improvements in Amtrak passenger train service, lead pipe repairs, port and airport funding, and public school improvements, among other long-awaited projects.</p><p>Democratic House Speaker Nancy Pelosi of California is seeking to have a bill passed sometime in July, but the legislation&#39;s fate also rests in the hands of the Senate, which the party only narrowly controls.</p><p>While Biden is seeking Republican input on the bill, Democrats <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/22361959/biden-infrastructure-jobs-plan-congress\">have not ruled out</a> passing an infrastructure package through the reconciliation process, which would only require a party-line vote.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Meet the Press  (@MeetThePress) <a with &#34;a combination of massive tax increases on businesses and individuals, and more borrowing.&#34;</p><p>&#34;I think that package they&#39;re putting together now, as much as we would like to Chase","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/digital-banking-trends-to-expect-from-head-of-digital-chase-2021-3","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60677a4da7d803001963e944?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Allison Beer\" height=\"1428\" width=\"1905\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Allison Beer is the head of customer experience and digital for Chase.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Allison Beer</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><a href=\"https://media.chase.com/leadership/gordon-smith/allison-beer\">Allison Beer</a> is chief product officer and head of customer experience and digital for Chase.</li>\n<li>She says the pandemic has accelerated changes in consumers&#39; digital banking needs.</li>\n<li>Over the next year, Beer says, there will be increased demand for personalization, automation, and real-time payments.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The last year changed all industries, including banking.</p><p>Consumers have embraced digital banking tools for several years, but the pandemic accelerated adoption even further across demographics. For example, half of Chase&#39;s new digitally active customers since March 2020 are over 50.  </p><p>New research suggests that we can expect consumers to engage more actively with their bank&#39;s digital offerings in 2021 and beyond. According to a recent <a href=\"https://www.jpmorgan.com/insights/technology/2020-digital-banking-survey\">Chase survey</a>, 80% of respondents prefer to manage their finances digitally rather than in-person.</p><p>We believe this preference will continue to increase demand for personalization, automation and real-time payments as consumers continue to shy away from cash. </p><h2><strong>Personalization</strong></h2><p>Every year, tech companies release new devices, hardware and software that allow consumers to update and personalize their experience. Consumers want the same experience from their bank.</p><p>Banking will become even more personalized in 2021, helping foster deeper engagement between customers and the features and services that their bank offers. </p><p>Advanced technologies - like artificial intelligence - can help banks create more customized experiences that adapt to each customer&#39;s individual needs. For example, people can already use their mobile banking app to enjoy offers and rewards from some of their favorite retailers and brands. Customers can also view unique insights about their spending and savings trends or credit score to make more informed financial decisions. </p><h2><strong>Automation</strong></h2><p>In a post-vaccine world, consumers will still want to find the most convenient and effective ways to manage their finances. We expect digital resources that assist with budgeting and bill payments to play a major role in future digital banking enhancements.</p><p>Automation, especially for payments and savings, has made it effortless for consumers to stay on top of their finances. Essentially, they increasingly want to use their mobile apps to &#34;set it and forget it.&#34; Moving forward, we anticipate that we will make an even wider array of automated tools available. </p><h2><strong>Real-time</strong></h2><p>Digital payments became even more popular last year, as consumers relied on safe, convenient and contactless methods for completing real-time peer to peer (P2P) payments. In fact, in 2020, the Zelle Network processed more than <a href=\"https://www.zellepay.com/press-releases/zeller-closes-2020-record-307-billion-sent-12-billion-transactions\">1.2 billion transactions</a> totaling $307 billion in payments. Consumers and businesses can easily process transactions using a variety of real-time payment platforms - whether they are paying rent, splitting a dinner bill, or paying the babysitter.</p><p>The early adopters of this technology were younger generations, but in 2020 we saw older customers use this way of paying more frequently. Real-time payments will undoubtedly grow in popularity as both consumers and businesses become more comfortable with the convenience and security it provides. </p><p>Digital banking will further influence who consumers choose to bank with. COVID-19 has increased customer preference for the convenience and speed that digital banking offers through websites and apps. To better serve consumers of all ages, banks will need to be agile enough to react quickly to the evolving needs of their customers.</p><p>At the end of the day, who consumers choose to bank with will increasingly depend on how easy it is for them to manage their entire financial life digitally from one place. Banks that make that experience seamless, insightful and simple will gain loyal customers who engage more frequently with their products and services.</p><p><a href=\"https://media.chase.com/leadership/gordon-smith/allison-beer\"><em>Allison Beer</em></a><em> is chief product officer and head of customer experience and digital for Chase. She&#39;s been with Chase since 2017. </em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a It was located in one wall of the 77-acre pond that holds about 600 million gallons of water, containing phosphorus, nitrogen, and small amounts of radium and uranium.</p><p>The stacks can also release large concentrations of radon gas.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moving-to-florida-texas-lower-cost-of-living-healthcare-medicaid-2021-3\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">People flocked to Florida and Texas for a lower cost of living during the pandemic. But this process is time-consuming and can take up to 12 days. </p><p>The governor, however, has ordered more pumps and cranes to be transported to the area.</p><p>Some workers tried to plug the hole with rocks and other materials on Friday afternoon but were unsuccessful. </p><p>George Kruse, a Manatee County commissioner, said he traveled to the plant on Saturday to assess the situation but had to leave the area quickly after realizing it was a safety hazard.</p><p>&#34;We determined that it was no longer safe to be anywhere near Piney Point, so we all kind of raced off the stacks as fast as we could,&#34; Kruse said, according to the Guardian.</p><p><a href=\"https://thebradentontimes.com/piney-points-timebomb-continues-to-tick-p20532-158.htm\">According to local media reports</a>, residents in the area have been trying to sound the alarm on the old phosphate plans for years.</p><p>The problem goes back to 1989, where a 23,000-gallon leak of sulfuric acid from a holding tank by the pond forced the evacuation of hundreds of nearby residents.</p><p>DeSantis in his Sunday press conference stressed that water quality is not so big a point of concern.</p><p>&#34;The water quality issues that are flowing through this for us is less than the risk of everyone&#39;s health and safety, particularly for those who live in the area,&#34; he said. </p><p>The governor also said 316 homes near the area have so far been evacuated, and safety notices have gone out to businesses as well. </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>Soldiers were suspended at Fort Sill in Oklahoma following a report of sexual assaults.</li> \n <li>The Intercept reported a female soldier accused 22 troops of being involved in the assaults.</li> \n <li>Reports of sexual assault in the military have risen sharply in the past two years.</li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider's business page</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>After a report of sexual assaults, a \"cadre\" of soldiers at Fort Sill in Oklahoma have been suspended while an investigation is carried out, the commanding general of the Army base said.</p>\n<p>A female soldier at the base reported on March 27 that \"she was the victim of sexual assault involving Fort Sill cadre members,\" Major General Ken Kamper said in a <a href=\"https://sill-www.army.mil/assets/docs/home/CG%20Opening%20Remarks.pdf\">statement</a> Thursday. He said the allegations were immediately reported to law enforcement and investigators began conducting interviews.</p>\n<p>\"This soldier, who came forward with allegations of sexual assault, is absolutely safe,\" Kamper said. \"We're proud of the courage she displayed in coming forward with these allegations.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/key-lessons-from-retired-army-sergeant-for-running-a-business\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">5 key lessons a retired Army sergeant picked up from his 34-year military career that have guided him as a successful entrepreneur</a></em></p>\n<p>The statement did not say how many soldiers were accused or suspended, but a military official told <a href=\"https://theintercept.com/2021/04/02/female-soldier-sexual-assault-22-troops-fort-sill/\">The Intercept</a> allegations were made against 22 soldiers and include multiple incidents of assault.</p>\n<p>The official also told The Intercept investigators were looking into a video of one of the incidents that was being passed around the base, but a US Army spokesperson denied that investigators had such a video.</p>\n<p>The group implicated in the allegations was \"suspended from their normal duties\" and \"removed from any trainee environment,\" Kamper said. They typically were involved in training new troops. The woman who came forward was a trainee.</p>\n<p>Sexual assault in the military is an ongoing issue, with assaults rising sharply in the past two years, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lloyd-austin-give-hope-to-survivors-of-sexual-assault-in-us-military-2021-2\">Insider's Sophia Ankel</a> reported.</p>\n<p>As one of his first acts after being confirmed in January, Defense Secretary Lloyd Austin ordered a review of how the department handles reports of sexual assault.</p>\n<p>The issue was given additional attention last year after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/missing-soldier-killed-at-armory-hammer-vanessa-guillen-2020-7\">US Army soldier Vanessa Guillen</a> was murdered at her base in Fort Hood, Texas. Guillen's family members said she had told them she experienced sexual harassment, but was too afraid to report it.</p>\n<p><em>Have a news tip? Data including his name, location, marriage details, birth date, and Facebook user ID was exposed, according to <a href=\"https://www.thesun.co.uk/news/14540292/mark-zuckerberg-facebook-data-breach-500-million-users/\">The Sun</a>. </p><p>Insider&#39;s Aaron Holmes <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stolen-data-of-533-million-facebook-users-leaked-online-2021-4\">had previously reported</a> on the leak, which involved the personal information of more than 500 million Facebook users being posted in the forum.</p><p>Cyber researcher Dave Walker said Zuckerberg, as well as Facebook co-founders Chris Hughes and Dustin Moskovitz, were among the 533 million users who had personal data posted on the forum. </p><p>&#34;Regarding the <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/FacebookLeak?src=hashtag_click\" data-focusable=\"true\">#FacebookLeak</a>, of the 533M people in the leak - the irony is that Mark Zuckerberg is regrettably included in the leak as well,&#34; Walker tweeted.</p><p>When Insider contacted Facebook on Sunday, a spokesperson said: &#34;This is old data that was previously reported on in 2019. We found and fixed this issue in August 2019.&#34; They did not comment on the reports about Zuckerberg&#39;s information. </p><p>Holmes reported, however, that the posting of the entire dataset on the hacking forum for free could now make it widely available to anyone with rudimentary data skills. His report quoted Alon Gal, CTO of cybercrime intelligence firm <a href=\"https://www.hudsonrock.com/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"b6dba036b340e59d888ca72f3971227b\">Hudson Rock</a>, who <a href=\"https://twitter.com/UnderTheBreach/status/1378314424239460352\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"4dfdb9f17fbcfdfa3fb44477bd529f08\">first discovered the entire trough of leaked data</a> online on Saturday.</p><p>Previous Facebook privacy breaches include the much-publicized Cambridge Analytica saga. In that incident, personal data from over <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/07/25/facebook-ignored-staff-warnings-about-sketchy-cambridge-analytica-in-september-2015/\">87 million Facebook users</a> was improperly obtained by the political data-analytics firm.</p><p>Facebook was hit with a $5 billion fine from the Federal Trade Commission as part of a settlement over claims the company mishandled user data.</p><p>The company has vowed to clamp down on data breaches. <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/news/cracking-down-on-platform-abuse\">In a post on its website</a> in the wake of the Cambridge Analytica revelations, it said it would take action on potential past abuse and put stronger protections in place to prevent future abuse.</p><p> </p><figure data-mod=\"image\" I dipped in and compared KFC&#39;s new line of sauces against Chick-fil-A&#39;s lineup to see who is the best.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tKFC sent me its line of new sauces in anticipation of its launch at all US restaurants on October 12.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa579391df1d500182194a5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KFC Sauce\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI ordered a four-pack of the chain's extra crispy tenders to dunk into the dipping sauces.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5798f1df1d500182194ab?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chicken Tenders\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI also ordered four-piece chicken strips from Chick-fil-A.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa579e31df1d500182194ad?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chick fil A\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tTo kick things off, I tried KFC's new \"Honey BBQ\" sauce.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57b0e1df1d500182194b9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KFC\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe sauce was sweet and lived up to the \"honey\" in its name. It tasted fine, but the flavor was pretty tame.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57b471df1d500182194bc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KFC\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tNext, I tried Chick-fil-A's barbecue sauce.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57b85f7d1cb0019e3a39b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chick-fil-A\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThis was closer to a traditional barbecue sauce found at a grill out.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57bd21df1d500182194c2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"CHICK FIL A\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe flavor was less sweet and relied more on savory-smokey tones. But it was still pretty muted and didn't have any spice or pepperiness to it.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57bff1df1d500182194c5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS9.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tBetween KFC and Chick-fil-A, the barbecue sauces were tied. Picking one just depends on whether you're in the mood for sweet or savory.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57c96f7d1cb0019e3a3a9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS10.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tFor my second round of sauces, I went for KFC's honey mustard.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57cbaf7d1cb0019e3a3aa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS11.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tKFC's honey mustard had a tiny hint of sharpness.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57ce3f7d1cb0019e3a3ac?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS12.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tBut mostly, it was a watery-consistency and didn't taste out of the ordinary.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57d041df1d500182194d0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS13.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tChick-fil-A's honey mustard was sweeter in comparison to KFC's version of the sauce.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57d261df1d500182194d1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS14.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIt had a brownish-yellow tone and a vinegary-consistency.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57d601df1d500182194d5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS15.JPG\" height=\"2661\" width=\"3992\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tStill, it was nothing out of the ordinary. They were both just okay.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57db2f7d1cb0019e3a3b9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS16.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tUp next was KFC's \"classic\" ranch.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57dcf1df1d500182194d9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS17.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe sauce hit all the checkpoints I look for in a homemade ranch.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa57decf7d1cb0019e3a3ba?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS18.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe consistency was buttery and thick.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a743f7d1cb0019e3a4bc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS19.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThere was a slight lactic-milk taste, but the herb mix was strong enough to contrast it with an oniony-kick.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a770f7d1cb0019e3a4be?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS20.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tOverall, it met my Midwestern obsession for high-quality ranch.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a7bbf7d1cb0019e3a4bf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS21.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI cracked open Chick-fil-A's \"Garden Herb Ranch,\" and while it was good, it didn't live up to the KFC version.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a7d91df1d500182195d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS22.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIt still had a nice, herby-zing to it, but the sauce was thinner.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a80a1df1d500182195da?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS23.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIf I brought KFC's ranch to a Super Bowl party, people would be thanking me.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a83ff7d1cb0019e3a4ca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS24.JPG\" height=\"2661\" width=\"3992\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tFinally, I popped open KFC's new house sauce.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a8c21df1d500182195df?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS25.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe KFC sauce tasted similar to a honey mustard with subtle hints of a smokey barbecue sauce.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a8e0f7d1cb0019e3a4cd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS26.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tKFC Sauce isn't thick, but it's still packed with contrasting flavors that made each dip delightful.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a925f7d1cb0019e3a4cf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS27.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI enjoyed it more than the other KFC sauces and expect it to become a popular addition for tender dippers everywhere.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a95df7d1cb0019e3a4d2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS28.JPG\" height=\"2661\" width=\"3992\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tNext up, I compared it to the iconic Chick-fil-A sauce.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a98b1df1d500182195e6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS29.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tBoth Chick-fil-A Sauce and KFC Sauce have a similar taste profile: Sweet, yet smokey. Tangy, but sharp. They were also similar in color.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a9f7f7d1cb0019e3a4d6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS30 (1).JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tChick-fil-A sauce was a tad bit sweeter, but the flavor was bolder than KFC's offering.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5aa2d1df1d500182195ea?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS31.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIt also tasted like a sweet barbecue sauce mixed with sharp mustard.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5aa83f7d1cb0019e3a4da?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS32.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIts satisfyingly thick consistency and sweet, honey taste made Chick-fil-A Sauce absolutely addictive and superior to KFC Sauce.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5aacd1df1d500182195eb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS33.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tOverall, the honey mustard and barbecue sauces from both chains were on par with each other.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5ab2af7d1cb0019e3a4e0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS34.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tKFC's creamy ranch was definitely superior to Chick-fil-A's offering.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5a743f7d1cb0019e3a4bc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS19.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tBut if you put Chick-fil-A Sauce and KFC Sauce head-to-head, there is no doubt the beloved yellow sauce packet is still at the top of the pecking order.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5aba9f7d1cb0019e3a4e2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS36.JPG\" height=\"2661\" width=\"3992\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe sauce's unique honey mustard and barbecue blend made me want to dunk my pizza into it, or maybe even drizzle it on a salad.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5ac0df7d1cb0019e3a4e6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KS37.JPG\" height=\"2661\" width=\"3992\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tBut while KFC's attempt to match its growing rival fell short, all of the new sauces, including KFC Sauce, are still dunk-worthy.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5ac491df1d500182195f0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"IMG_0688.JPG\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p REUTERS/Brendan McDermid/File Photo\" height=\"2433\" width=\"3244\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Carl Icahn.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Billionaire fund manager Carl Icahn has named Aris Kekedjian as CEO of Icahn Enterprises, the WSJ reported.</li>\n<li>Kekedjian, who will assume the CEO post on Monday, previously spent three decades at GE.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/carl-icahn-stock-market-outlook-wild-rallies-major-painful-correction-2021-1-1029931343\">Billionaire fund manager Carl Icahn</a> has named a former General Electric executive as CEO of Icahn Enterprises, the <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/carl-icahn-taps-former-ge-executive-to-be-ceo-of-his-firm-11617528601?mod=hp_lead_pos2\">Wall Street Journal</a> reported Sunday.</p><p>In an interview with the Journal, the activist investor said Aris Kekedjian will take over as CEO and chief operating officer on Monday. Kekedjian spent three decades at GE, and was the company&#39;s chief investment officer until 2019, the Journal reported.</p><p>Icahn Enterprises current CEO, Keith Cozza, and chief financial officer, SungHwan Cho, are leaving the firm, which consists of Icahn&#39;s investment fund and other companies he controls, the WSJ said.</p><p>Icahn told the newspaper the pair of top executives were leaving on excellent terms. The decision was partly precipitated because neither planned to relocate to the Miami area, where Icahn Enterprises moved last year, he said.  </p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/carl-icahn-moving-hedge-fund-to-miami-from-new-york-2019-9-1028523239\">In 2019, Icahn told staff</a> he was shutting down offices in New York and opening up in early 2020 in Miami. Those who stayed with the company received moving expenses. Those who didn&#39;t want to move to Florida got severance, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-people-icahn/billionaire-investor-carl-icahn-to-leave-new-york-for-florida-idUSKCN1VY02I\">Reuters</a> and the New York Post reported. </p><p>Over the past year, a number of other <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/wall-street-move-florida-goldman-sachs-elliott-real-estate-2020-12\">powerful tech titans and Wall Street heavyweights </a>have also made the move to Florida, drawn by lower taxes and other perks. Remote work during the COVID-19 pandemic also spurred some <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/a-list-of-all-the-powerful-people-moving-to-florida-right-now-2021-1\">companies and powerful individuals </a>to consider the move. </p><p>Icahn Enterprises did not immediately respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment about Kekedjian.</p><p> </p><p> </p><p> </p><div 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"The Biden administration ramps up their effort to address hunger in America, relieving a burden on millions of Americans","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-administration-ramps-up-efforts-to-address-hunger-2021-4","description":"<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606a51d6856cd700198a3165?format=jpeg\" alt=\"food bank drive thru\" height=\"745\" width=\"1490\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption> \n   <p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/search/photographer?family=editorial&amp;photographer=Miami+Herald\" target=\"_blank\">Miami Herald/Getty Images</a></p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>President Joe Biden's administration is ramping efforts to address food insecurity and hunger. </li> \n <li>They authorized the largest children's summer feeding program in history, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/04/us/politics/biden-hunger-programs.html\">The New York Times</a> said. </li> \n <li>The administration also expanded SNAP benefits and resources for children.</li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider's business page</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>President Joe Biden's administration is rapidly increasing aid to ramp up their efforts to address the hunger crisis in America, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/04/us/politics/biden-hunger-programs.html\">The New York Times</a> reported. </p>\n<p>In January, Biden signed executive orders to help families get the food that they need. He asked the Department of Agriculture and Congress to <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/statements-releases/2021/01/22/fact-sheet-president-bidens-new-executive-actions-deliver-economic-relief-for-american-families-and-businesses-amid-the-covid-19-crises/\">consider expanding and extending federal nutrition assistance programs</a>, including the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-will-implement-executive-actions-to-provide-relief-to-americans-2021-1\">Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program and the Pandemic Electronic Benefits Transfer</a> which help children get meals they missed by being out of school. </p>\n<p>According to the <a href=\"https://www.cbpp.org/research/poverty-and-inequality/tracking-the-covid-19-recessions-effects-on-food-housing-and\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"99240ab5026c25e387d3c3bd7349d7f4\">Center on Budget and Policy Priorities</a>, 22 million adults - 11 percent of all adults in the country - struggled to obtain the food they needed in the past week, including one in six households with children. </p>\n<p>The Times reported that the administration has so far authorized the largest children's summer feeding program in history, giving over $1 billion a month in increased food stamps and needy kids $1 a day for snacks. It also expanded a produce allowance for pregnant women and children.</p>\n<p>\"We haven't seen an expansion of food assistance of this magnitude since the founding of the modern food stamp program in 1977,\" James P. Ziliak, an economist at the University of Kentucky who studies nutrition programs, told the Times. \"It's a profound change.\"</p>\n<p>The pandemic has financially impacted millions of families, with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/food-banks-feeding-americans-unemployment-hunger-2020-4\">many needing to rely on food banks</a> with long lines and demands they were unable to always meet. </p>\n<p>Dakota Kirby, 29, a single mother of two kids who lost her job at the start of the pandemic, told The Times she was struggling to make her $509 a month in food stamps last past three weeks and would have to ration her food to ensure her kids are fed. </p>\n<p>The new measures have since given her family $930 a month from three support programs, or $10 a day for each person. </p>\n<p>\"That's a big old jump!\" she said, surprised at the news. \"It will help tremendously.\"</p>\n<p><em>Have a news tip? It has been an increasing concern for celebrities and public figures. <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/aoc-calls-revenge-porn-targeting-rep-katie-hill-major-crime-2019-10\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">It especially affects women</a>.</p><p>Many experts say the name &#34;revenge porn&#34; is misleading because it implies the victim must have done something to deserve the crime when this is almost always not the case, <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/katie-hill-revenge-porn-consent-exploitation-2019-11\">Insider reported
