fe.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-06-748_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=35np-vVKy5Y:1XiLDbUys5c:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn8@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-04-885_dd3123bc13a6391c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/35np-vVKy5Y":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn85@2020_1/2021/04/05/06-46-06-212_c8e7dbd99e304a18.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617605114920},{"createdTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"Christians are increasingly falling victim to online falsehoods. Meet the librarian leading the fight against conspiracy theories and health misinformation.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/christians-are-often-victims-of-conspiracy-theories-health-falsehoods-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60659020daf0f10018f99658?format=jpeg\" alt=\"church mask phone\" height=\"2736\" width=\"5472\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A worshipper wearing a protective face mask checks her smartphone while attending a Sunday service on May 10, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Odd Andersen/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A librarian is leading the church&#39;s fight against <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pastors-quit-after-qanon-radicalize-congregation-2021-3\">misinformation</a> by holding online media workshops.</li>\n<li>Rachel Wightman is teaching church congregants to identify fake news, and fact-check their sources.</li>\n<li>White evangelicals are more likely to believe in conspiracy theories, recent polls show.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A local librarian from <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/800000-vaccinated-people-in-minnesota-only-89-got-covid-19-2021-3\">Minnesota</a> is leading the fight against <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pastors-quit-after-qanon-radicalize-congregation-2021-3\">misinformation in Christian churches</a> by holding online media training for congregations across the country.</p><p>Rachel Wightman works full-time at Concordia University, St.Paul, but started teaching six-week seminars part-time after watching a worrying number of people in her community became misguided by online misinformation.</p><p>The presidential election prompted Wightman to give her first workshop at her local Mill City Church in Minneapolis in early 2020. But the coronavirus pandemic paired with the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/george-floyd-protests-defining-history-politics-election-black-lives-matter-2020-6\">Black Lives Matter protests</a> made her workshops a lot more pertinent, so she decided to organize more.</p><p>The BLM movement, in particular, hit close to home - Wightman&#39;s church was only a few miles away from where <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/uk-protests-black-lives-matter-police-statues-2020-7\">George Floyd was killed</a>, and for most of the summer months, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/13-concrete-changes-sparked-by-george-floyd-protests-so-far-2020-6\">the city was gripped by protests.</a></p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/california-pastor-risks-arrest-million-dollar-fines-church-mask-services-2021-2\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">HOLY WAR: A California pastor who believes ventilators are killing people is holding massive, mask-free services - and he refuses to shut down</a></em></p><p>&#34;I remember the day our pastor was talking about racism and saying we have to check our inputs, meaning we have to get inputs from people who are different in order to understand this issue,&#34; Wightman told Insider. &#34;That was the moment for me where it really clicked. I knew I had to continue giving people tools to get to these inputs.&#34;</p><p>In the last few weeks, the librarian has become inundated with requests from other pastors from around the US asking her to give her workshops to their congregations. </p><p>The need for such training seems to be as urgent as ever: Over the last year, churches have become engulfed in conspiracy theories and health misinformation, in some cases <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pastors-quit-after-qanon-radicalize-congregation-2021-3\">even prompting pastors to leave their congregations.</a></p><p>Recent polls show that white evangelicals have one of the highest levels of vaccine skepticism in the United States. According to a <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2021/02/16/covid-vaccine-misinformation-evangelical-mark-beast/\">Washington Post/ABC News</a> poll published in January,  just under a third of US adults say they will probably or definitely not get the vaccine, compared to 44% of those who identify as white evangelicals.</p><p>Another poll by the Christian research organization <a href=\"https://lifewayresearch.com/2021/01/26/half-of-u-s-protestant-pastors-hear-conspiracy-theories-in-their-churches/\">Lifeway Research</a> found that more than 45% of protestant pastors said they had often heard congregants repeating conspiracy theories.</p><p>&#34;As a librarian, I&#39;m seeing this huge information landscape every day, and I feel like it&#39;s incredibly overwhelming for people,&#34; Wightman said. &#34;We&#39;ve all spent this past year in this hyped-up environment where everything feels urgent and stressful, so I try to encourage people to take some space and say: &#39;Okay, I&#39;m going to figure out how to slow down and make sense of everything around me.&#39;&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606590b56183e10019819ad9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"rachel wightman librarian\" height=\"1239\" width=\"1653\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rachel Wightman, Associate Director for Instruction and Outreach at Concordia University in St. Paul, Minnesota.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Nick Schroepfer, Concordia University, St. Paul</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Due to the pandemic, Wightman meets most of her students on Zoom. Together they talk about everything from how to identify fake photographs, the ways in which algorithms work, fact-checking sources, and how to avoid being judgmental when friends post something inaccurate online.</p><p>Wightman stressed that while the training is a good space to talk about all the information people find online, it is also &#34;politically neutral.&#34; </p><p>&#34;We&#39;re not here to talk about your opinion on the latest legislation or our president. We are here to talk about how do you evaluate what you&#39;re finding online ... and how that overlaps with your faith,&#34; she said.</p><p>For the librarian, it is also important to keep faith at the center of her teachings.</p><p>&#34;I want to also bring in this perspective of Christianity. As Christians, we need to ask ourselves, if you have this faith of loving your neighbors, in what spaces does your faith show up?&#39;&#34;</p><p>The librarian said her workshops had been received well by many churchgoers, who vary in age and race. Many are also taking the training to help family members who have succumbed to online misinformation, Wightman said. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/604d0a6110c8760018b93198?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trump capitol religion\" height=\"1000\" width=\"1334\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Pro-Trump supporters storm the U.S. Capitol following a rally with President Donald Trump on January 6, 2021 in Washington, DC.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brent Stirton/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Dr. Christopher Douglas, a professor of English at the University of Victoria, specializing in Christian literature, politics, and epistemology, thinks having training is essential in this day and age.</p><p>&#34;Misinformation is in some sense baked into white evangelical churches as many of them reject science, scholarship, and mainstream journalism,&#34; Douglas told Insider. &#34;It&#39;s a small step from disputing the science of evolution and climate change to doubting the efficacy of masks and vaccines in fighting the pandemic because it all comes from a common source, which is mainstream &#39;secular&#39; science.&#34;</p><p>Douglas believes 2020&#39;s pandemic and election exacerbated this problem as many feel like their political opponents are trying to &#34;destroy Christian America and to take away what they call their &#39;religious freedoms.&#39;&#34;<u></u><u></u></p><p>This is why Christian churches need training like Wightman&#39;s, Douglas said. &#34;Public institutions like libraries, colleges, and universities all have a role to play in developing critical thinking and critical media literacy skills,&#34; he said.</p><p>Even though Wightman is balancing her new work with a full-time job, she said she&#39;s proud of what she&#39;s accomplished so far and hopes to continue doing more workshops in the future.</p><p>&#34;A lot of people think librarians just sit around and read all day, so it&#39;s been fun to bust that myth open a bit,&#34; said Wightman. &#34;We&#39;re teachers, we&#39;re about connecting people with information, and so be able to do that in a new way that feels so relevant is very exciting.&#34; </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Ankel)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60659020daf0f10018f99658?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn70@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-05-030_8d832de8764544a3.webp","https://i.insider.com/606590b56183e10019819ad9?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn10@2020_1/2021/04/05/06-46-10-858_ee0f3aac5cb5a945.webp","https://i.insider.com/604d0a6110c8760018b93198?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn90@2020_4/2021/04/05/06-46-07-952_76d0d3222df25127.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn6@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-09-303_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=bPxQLhYGcoo:XCFzQxqHnDU:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn81@2020_5/2021/04/05/06-46-08-870_1ecd489b898dadf9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=bPxQLhYGcoo:XCFzQxqHnDU:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn70@2020_2/2021/04/05/06-46-08-104_cf1df0ac26bb7a2f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-06-748_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=bPxQLhYGcoo:XCFzQxqHnDU:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn21@2020_2/2021/04/05/06-46-10-817_803063e89322ebe4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/bPxQLhYGcoo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn86@2020_2/2021/04/05/06-46-08-529_267dca8b07b9d903.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617605114906},{"createdTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"Fertility experts debunk 19 myths about getting pregnant and fertility","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/fertility-experts-debunk-19-fertility-pregnancy-myths-2021-3","description":"<div style=\"position:relative; overflow:hidden; padding-bottom:56.25%\">\n<iframe src=\"https://cdn.jwplayer.com/players/HPfWzE7P-jZbcmOYf.html\" width=\"100%\" height=\"100%\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"auto\" title=\"Fertility experts debunk 19 myths about getting pregnant and fertility\" style=\"position:absolute;\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n</div><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/fertility\">Fertility</a> specialist Cindy Duke and reproductive urologist Sriram Eleswarapu debunk common myths.</li>\n<li>They talk about how <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/ivf\">IVF</a> isn&#39;t guaranteed to work and how stress does not cause pregnancy loss.</li>\n<li>Dr. Duke and Dr. Eleswarapu dive deep into these <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/infertility\">infertility myths</a> on this episode of Debunked.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><strong>Duke: </strong>&#34;Sex position matters.&#34;</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu:</strong> So, that is a myth.</p><p>&#34;IVF guarantees pregnancy.&#34;</p><p><strong>Duke: </strong>Oh, boy. It&#39;s a tough myth for patients to hear.</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu: </strong>&#34;Eating pineapple can increase fertility.&#34;</p><p><strong>Duke: </strong>Oh, that&#39;s a good one. Pineapple by itself, if you have infertility, is unlikely to reverse your infertility.</p><p>I&#39;m Dr. Cindy. I am a fertility specialist based in Las Vegas, Nevada. Hello,</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu: </strong>I&#39;m Dr. Sriram Eleswarapu, and I&#39;m a urologist at UCLA. And today we&#39;ll be debunking myths about infertility.</p><p><strong>Duke:</strong> &#34;Tight underwear is bad for sperm count.&#34;</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu: </strong>So, there&#39;ve been a number of studies looking at this issue for many decades, and the inevitable question is boxers versus briefs. In truth, it doesn&#39;t matter a whole lot, and we know that if the testicles are a little bit warmer that they are more at risk of having sperm-count issues or sperm-motility issues, but, in general, it shouldn&#39;t matter too much. Just pick what&#39;s comfortable.</p><p><strong>Duke: </strong>&#34;Sex position matters.&#34;</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu: </strong>So, that is a myth. No matter what position you engage in, if you ejaculate, you have the sufficient propulsion of the semen to make it up to the cervix, any way you do it.</p><p><strong>Duke: </strong>People around the world have actually studied it, and no one position has been proven to be better than another.</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu: </strong>&#34;IVF guarantees pregnancy.&#34;</p><p><strong>Duke: </strong>Oh, boy. Yes, that is definitely a myth. And it&#39;s a tough myth for patients to hear. IVF does present the highest chances of pregnancy, absolutely. There are a number of factors that play into IVF success. One of them has to do with the age of the eggs being used. It also has to do with the quality of the sperm and the egg when they come together. It has to do with the embryo that is ultimately formed. It also has to do with the genetics of the embryo. But then, on top of that, it has to do with the womb in which the embryo will be placed, and a number of factors are not yet fully known. So, we know the immune system plays a role. Diet, exercise probably play a role, but we&#39;re still investigating that. Biggest thing to know is it&#39;s not 100%.</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu: </strong>&#34;Stress causes miscarriages.&#34;</p><p>I think we&#39;re starting to get away from the term &#34;miscarriages.&#34; We&#39;re starting to use the term &#34;early pregnancy loss.&#34; Is that right?</p><p><strong>Duke: </strong>That&#39;s correct. And I think it&#39;s because &#34;miscarriage&#34; also comes with certain connotations where blame is also ascribed, and the truth is, both early pregnancy losses, there&#39;s nothing the individual could have done about it at all. So now we call it early pregnancy loss before the end of the first trimester, versus second- and third-trimester pregnancy loss. We do not believe stress causes loss. Many people around the world across millennia have gotten pregnant and remain pregnant despite tremendous stress. So we know it&#39;s not simply stress. Nowadays, though, we know the No. 1 reason for pregnancy loss is chromosomal differences in the formed embryo. And so that&#39;s called aneuploidy. 67% of first-trimester pregnancy losses are due to chromosomal issues within the embryo itself. Other reasons would be if the thyroid was not functioning well, if vitamin D is low, if there&#39;s a fibroid in the uterus. If you have a uterus and you&#39;ve had two or more pregnancy losses, you should be evaluated. We always expected that it would be the individual with the womb and the eggs to be the one that gets evaluated for a pregnancy loss. Now the tide is shifting, and individuals who contribute the sperm are also being evaluated when there&#39;s a pregnancy loss in the couple. There&#39;s emerging data that things like DNA fragmentation, where the DNA that are normally supposed to be very tightly wrapped up in the sperm are somehow unraveled and might have little breaks in the DNA strands, and those breaks can contribute to the pregnancy loss.</p><p>&#34;Freezing your eggs guarantees that you can have kids later.&#34;</p><p>Myth. And the myth is in the word &#34;guaranteed.&#34; If you freeze your eggs, you can stop the clock. And so you&#39;re basically freezing the youngest version of yourself at that point. However, there&#39;s no guarantee that eggs even when frozen will thaw and yield a live-born baby. So it&#39;s really a conversation that needs to happen with your specialist based on your age, based on your egg number.</p><p>&#34;Sperm quality doesn&#39;t decline with age.&#34;</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu: </strong>There&#39;s a lot of data now that is showing that individuals with sperm that is older, say in the fifth, sixth, seventh decades of life and beyond, is more at risk of forming embryos that have chromosomal abnormalities. Getting exercise, eating well are things that can improve the general biology of an individual. Certainly if it&#39;s good for the heart and it&#39;s good for the brain, then it&#39;s probably good for the penis and the scrotum and the testicles as well. We talked about egg freezing, but sperm freezing has its role particularly for individuals who may not be in a relationship or may not be thinking of a family at this time but later on down the road they might want to produce a family.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s impossible to get pregnant after 35.&#34;</p><p><strong>Duke: </strong>It is possible to get pregnant after 35. The truth is, though, that the chance of pregnancy progressively declines as the age of the egg increases. And so you might find greater and greater need for fertility treatments. When you&#39;re born, if you&#39;re someone born with ovaries, you&#39;d have somewhere between 1 million to 2 million eggs in those ovaries, usually. By age 30, 70% of those eggs are gone, and by age 40, 97% of those eggs are gone. At the same time, those eggs are also aging. And so what we see is that the chance of pregnancy declines very quickly, and then for some people it declines even faster. So if you have endometriosis, if you&#39;re someone who&#39;s maybe had surgeries of the ovaries or needed to be on medications, chemotherapy, radiation, all of those things can also further the decline in the egg number. So my recommendation is, if you have ovaries, at age 30, you should at least be asking your doctor to do a check of your egg number, or what&#39;s called your ovarian reserve.</p><p>&#34;The best way to get pregnant is to have sex every day.&#34;</p><p><strong>Eleswarapu: </strong>It comes down to the ovulatory cycles and making sure that you&#39;re sort of timing things and tracking things, particularly if you&#39;re trying to conceive deliberately. We always get this question, and I want to know what your thoughts are. Should the couple be trying to conceive every other day during ovulation, or every day during ovulation? I say every other day. One, we need to give the sperm and semen enough time to sort of reaccumulate so we can get those millions of sperm. The other is sperm actually survive in the female genital tract for up to five days. So once the egg is released from the ovary, think of the fallopian tube as an arm with a catcher&#39;s mitt at the end. The catcher&#39;s mitt captures the egg, pulls it into the arm, and then the egg sits around there for 12 to 20 hours waiting for sperm. And then if you have intercourse anywhere within the next 24 hours, sperm will also get to the egg. So that&#39;s why we say every other day around ovulation. There is this movement now, particularly on the internet, discussing what&#39;s called abstinence from pornography, masturbation, and orgasm, or PMO. It&#39;s also a movement called no NoFap. And those individuals say to have the best reserve of sperm or the best sort of power with erections or orgasm, that they should conserve for days, weeks, months at a time. This stuff is not scientific at all. And, in fact, after a week of storing up, the sperm may not necessarily be healthy.</p><p>&#34;Eating pineapple can increase fertility.&#34;</p><p><strong>Duke: </strong>That&#39;s a good one. Pineapple by itself, if you have infertility, is unlikely to reverse your infertility. We know that pineapples have bromelain inside of them, which is a compound that is known to be a blood thinner to a certain degree, but it&#39;s very, very weak, and you&#39;d have to eat so much pineapple to even have enough bromelain to have a little effect. You should be having a meal balancing protein, complex carbohydrates, and fiber. So getting your usual multivitamins and folate into your diet, because folate is really important for once you&#39;re pregnant. But technically, no, pineapple by itself does not boost fertility. Infertility, while a daunting thought, really there are lots of options available. The first step is actually an evaluation. Fertility and infertility constitute this huge spectrum, and there are many, many ways to get pregnant and many things one can do to help facilitate that. And you don&#39;t have to stay at home feeling embarrassed about it. If you talk to a specialist like myself, like Dr. Eleswarapu, we are experienced with this and know how to treat you or direct you to the right person who can help.</p><div height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 04 Apr 2021 20:15:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/6058a8e81fcb5700186eea8d?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"2614a15ad7224765d98ebe1562e9eda9","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn93@2020_4/2021/04/05/06-46-03-010_6d6840c68247de4b.webp","destWidth":1440,"destHeight":1080,"sourceBytes":42526,"destBytes":42526,"author":"atang@businessinsider.com (Abby Tang,Michelle Yan Huang,Ally Giannini)","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn6@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-09-303_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=gTcBeZY_XEg:CX_wKuKpGaE:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn34@2020_5/2021/04/05/06-46-06-554_0a5cf741fb4bdf8e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=gTcBeZY_XEg:CX_wKuKpGaE:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn95@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-05-455_195e5a37f0223d9b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-06-748_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=gTcBeZY_XEg:CX_wKuKpGaE:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn24@2020_1/2021/04/05/06-46-04-440_2d45e8b999b581e3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/gTcBeZY_XEg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn19@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-03-329_3606d7e6febef1b6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617605114842},{"createdTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"Biden's infrastructure plan does not come close to tackling the vast extent of America's new housing crisis","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/bidens-infrastructure-plan-not-enough-tackle-new-american-housing-crisis-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6065ff1852f11d00194319f9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Housing crisis homeless camp Philadelphia\" height=\"2258\" width=\"3011\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Activists outside a homeless camp in Philadelphia on September 9, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Cory Clark/NurPhoto via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The pandemic has exacerbated the existing housing crisis, and Biden&#39;s plan does not go far enough. </li>\n<li>There is no safety net for housing, making any assistance during economic recessions difficult to deliver. </li>\n<li>The crisis was built by poor government policy. The current administration must take steps to ensure housing as a basic human right. </li>\n<li><strong>Lindsay Owens</strong> is the interim Executive Director of the Groundwork Collaborative.</li>\n<li><strong>Sammi Aibinder </strong>is Special Assistant at the Groundwork Collaborative.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the authors.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The spending plans that the Biden administration released this week laid out substantial investments into our nation&#39;s housing system, <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/statements-releases/2021/03/31/fact-sheet-the-american-jobs-plan/?utm_source=NLIHC+All+Subscribers&utm_campaign=a07780d36a-CTA_033121&utm_medium=email&utm_term=0_e090383b5e-a07780d36a-291651401&ct=t(CTA_033121)ct=t(CTA_033121)\">including</a> $213 billion for building and retrofitting affordable housing units, $40 billion for public housing capital repairs, and grant funding to address zoning laws rooted in <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/22252625/america-racist-housing-rules-how-to-fix\">racial and economic exclusion</a>. These proposals are a welcome first step to ensuring safe, affordable, sustainable shelter - and Congress should move swiftly to enact them  - but they do not come close to meeting the scale of the housing crisis that has been underway in the United States for decades.</p><p>The reality is that although the failures in our housing system were exacerbated by the pandemic - to the tune of 10 million people at risk of eviction and<a href=\"https://www.moodysanalytics.com/-/media/article/2021/averting-an-eviction-crisis.pdf\"> more than $57 billion</a> owed in back rent - the pandemic didn&#39;t cause them. Rents have been soaring for decades, consuming an ever larger share of the incomes of the lowest-income Americans (and during the pandemic, the divergence in rent for low-income tenants versus higher-income tenants has<a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/2021/03/22/rents-rich-are-plummeting-rents-poor-are-rising-why/?itid=ap_catherinerampell\"> worsened</a>). </p><p>While renter incomes grew by 0.5% from 2001 to 2018,<a href=\"https://www.cbpp.org/blog/census-income-rent-gap-grew-in-2018\"> rents increased by 13%</a>. Median asking rent has<a href=\"https://www.census.gov/housing/hvs/files/currenthvspress.pdf\"> more than doubled</a> over the last 20 years, and in<a href=\"https://reports.nlihc.org/sites/default/files/oor/OOR_BOOK_2020.pdf\"> 95% of counties</a>, a full-time minimum-wage worker cannot afford to rent a one-bedroom apartment. Black and brown people are<a href=\"https://urbn.is/2yyrmsq\"> particularly vulnerable</a> to the extreme instability renters face. With a housing market this fragile during boom times, Americans never stood a chance when a crisis inevitably hit.</p><h2><strong>No housing safety net</strong></h2><p>It doesn&#39;t have to be this way. The economic impact of recessions, such as job losses and income declines, are largely predictable, and policymakers have put in place a number of programs to offset them. When Americans lose their jobs, they can apply for unemployment insurance; when their income and assets drop below a certain threshold, they qualify for nutritional assistance. </p><p>But when it comes to housing, there&#39;s no comparable safety net. The federal government currently offers no guaranteed form of housing assistance, and there are no countercyclical housing programs that expand during downturns or are triggered by economic indicators. This makes it almost impossible to quickly and effectively deliver any assistance that Congress <em>does</em> allocate during a disaster like this one. Variations in application and eligibility requirements across states and cities have led to backlogs in distribution of federal aid money, all while thousands upon thousands of applicants have been <a href=\"https://www.thecity.nyc/2020/12/22/22196601/new-york-rent-relief-expansion-still-strands-many\">denied assistance</a>.</p><p>The fragility of our housing market is <a href=\"https://groundworkcollaborative.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/PastDueHousingPolicy_Final.pdf\">not an accident; policy choices have led to a two-tiered housing market</a> in which relatively well-off, mostly white consumers can achieve the American dream of homeownership - with the help of considerable federal subsidies like the mortgage interest tax deduction - while renters, who are disproportionately Black, brown, and low-income, transfer an increasingly large share of their income to landlords in the private market. Ultimately, the scarcity of affordable and accessible housing in our economy is not reflective of national resources - it is reflective of a centuries-long political debate about who is deserving of public investment, and therefore economic dignity and security.</p><p>Consider the federal budget for housing programs geared toward those with the lowest incomes. Federal spending on housing assistance relative to gross domestic product has<a href=\"https://www.cbpp.org/research/housing/chart-book-cuts-in-federal-assistance-have-exacerbated-families-struggles-to\"> fallen by 30% </a>since the mid-1990s. Funding for public housing in particular has suffered profound losses: in the last 20 years<a href=\"https://www.cbpp.org/research/housing/chart-book-cuts-in-federal-assistance-have-exacerbated-families-struggles-to\"> the annual federal budget</a> has only met operations needs for public housing across the country three times. On top of that, funding for repairs has been cut in half - a trend that can&#39;t be divorced from the long-standing political tradition of pathologizing poor and low-income Black communities. This continued disinvestment has resulted in the<a href=\"https://www.jchs.harvard.edu/sites/default/files/reports/files/Harvard_JCHS_The_State_of_the_Nations_Housing_2020_Report_Revised_120720.pdf\"> share of households receiving housing assistance declining to just one in five</a> today. As the rental affordability crisis has worsened, the federal response has shrunk.</p><p>Meanwhile,<a href=\"https://www.cbpp.org/research/housing/chart-book-federal-housing-spending-is-poorly-matched-to-need\"> recent estimates</a> have shown that more than two-thirds of the government&#39;s total spending on housing is allocated toward subsidizing homeowners through tax deductions. The vast majority of benefits from this &#34;entitlement&#34; go to the wealthiest of households, and most Black and brown families are excluded entirely. By structuring housing policy and housing markets so that Americans&#39; homes are their most valuable asset and source of equity, this country has essentially transferred safety net functions to private homeowners (and enabled white families to maintain wealth by passing down the homes they own over generations). </p><h2><strong>Calling on the Biden administration</strong></h2><p>Our government can make different choices. Housing policies that rely on the private market to develop, administer, or maintain housing stock for those who are housing insecure have not come close to meeting the need for millions of people, because genuinely affordable housing is not profitable. If the Biden administration wants to truly &#34;Build Back Better&#34; and deliver on the <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/legislation/2021/01/20/president-biden-announces-american-rescue-plan/\">promise</a> of stable housing for all, it must commit to massive, sustained public investments, and a significant shift in our narrative around who is deserving of those investments.</p><p>There is no one silver-bullet solution: a number of approaches must be taken at the federal, state, and local levels (both regulatory <em>and</em> budgetary) to put us on the path toward an equitable and resilient housing system. Experts across the field, including grassroots leaders, researchers, and policymakers, have laid out<a href=\"https://communitychange.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/New-Deal-for-Housing-Justice.Policy-Paper.Community-Change.1.2020.pdf\"> extensive</a><a href=\"https://homesguarantee.com/wp-content/uploads/Homes-Guarantee-_-Briefing-Book.pdf\"> agendas</a> for these actions. The Biden campaign previously committed to <a href=\"https://joebiden.com/housing/\">fully funding rental assistance</a> for all who qualify - another important start, but one that does not adequately address permanent solutions to housing unaffordability. </p><p>In addition to advancing legislation that, at an absolute minimum, meets the Biden administration&#39;s priorities for housing, Congress must move to repeal the Faircloth Amendment, which has prohibited any increase to public housing stock since its passage over 20 years ago. Congress and the White House must also enact policies and fund programs that prioritize rehabilitation and preservation - not demolition - of homes in disinvested neighborhoods. Keeping new and revitalized homes affordable will also mean a strong commitment to rent control policies that place strict limits on rent increases, as well as exploration of alternative social and collective<a href=\"https://shelterforce.org/2018/07/30/solutions-to-an-unjust-housing-system/\"> ownership</a><a href=\"https://jacobinmag.com/2019/07/community-land-trusts-affordable-housing\"> models</a> that empower tenants and grant them the dignity and security of stable housing.</p><p>The path forward isn&#39;t easy, but the lessons from history are clear. We are long past due for a major course correction in our federal housing policy: not just to patch things up in case of emergency, but to remedy longstanding inequities and recognize shelter as a basic right in the wealthiest country in the world.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/bidens-infrastructure-plan-not-enough-tackle-new-american-housing-crisis-2021-4'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a the matter.</p><p>Despite chief executive officer Thomas Gottstein&#39;s commitment to a clean slate in 2021, after a previous spying scandal at the bank, Credit Suisse has been one of the worst-performing major bank stocks in 2021.</p><p>The recent collapse of Greensill, along with chaos at Archegos, has potentially left investors facing another quarter of losses.</p><p>The role of Brian Chin, CEO of Credit Suisse&#39;s investment bank, is also under scrutiny, two of the sources told Bloomberg. A $140 million collateralized loan to Greensill is now in default, although $50 million has been recently repaid by administrators, Bloomberg reported.</p><p>This is essentially pooled debt that is taken to market via a single security. Investors receive scheduled payments from the loans but assume most of the risk in the event that borrowers default.</p><p>The Swiss bank&#39;s asset management unit also ran a $10 billion group of funds with Greensill, which are being wound down.</p><p>On Monday, the Swiss firm had $4.8 billion wiped from its market capitalization on Monday. Its shares tumbled as much as 14% when the bank <a href=\"https://www.credit-suisse.com/about-us-news/en/articles/media-releases/trading-update-us-based-hedge-fund-202103.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">warned</a> it could suffer a major blow to its first-quarter profits after Archegos, a US-based hedge fund liquidated.</p><p>It said the losses could be &#34;highly significant and material&#34; to its first-quarter earnings, due next month.</p><p>Archegos, the family office of trader Bill Hwang, was forced to liquidate <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-wall-street-speculating-hedge-fund-liquidation-archegos-2021-3?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">more than $20 billion</a> of leveraged equity positions last week. The fire sale hammered stocks such as ViacomCBS and Baidu, and set off alarms at multiple Wall Street banks.</p><p>The bank could face a loss of $3 billion to $4 billion, <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/073509cd-fe45-44d2-afac-cace611b6900\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the Financial Times reported</a>, citing two sources. The top end of that estimate would be almost triple its net income in the first quarter of 2020. From the Archegos trades, the banking sector could take a collective hit of up to $10 billion, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/archegos-banks-10-billion-losses-liquidation-jpmorgan-nomura-credit-suisse-2021-3-1030260529\">JPMorgan analysts have estimated.</a></p><p>Bloomberg noted that this is only adding to the scrutiny on management, after several other miscues at the investment bank and beyond, including exposure to the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/lkncy-stock\" title=\"Company Overview\">Luckin Coffee Inc.</a> fraud.</p><aside></aside><p>Gottstein is expected to remain CEO, the people told Bloomberg.</p><p>The latest issues for the bank could also put its planned share buyback at risk, potentially pausing it for a second time, Bloomberg reported, as losses could threaten the bank&#39;s dividend distribution.</p><p>Credit Suisse declined to comment on the potential fallout of the trades.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/6069adbaa7d803001963ea6d?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"6f7927e7653e6a43f59091f05caca551","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn100@2020_5/2021/04/05/06-46-03-120_2da00cec2888884f.webp","destWidth":4969,"destHeight":3725,"sourceBytes":192682,"destBytes":192682,"author":"tgolden@businessinsider.com (Theo Golden)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f3c3a30b2fa21001d8daa29?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn62@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-10-135_4755594cda1fb765.webp","https://i.insider.com/6069b0d7856cd700198a3120?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn100@2020_2/2021/04/05/06-46-04-348_f886eb299a42139b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn6@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-09-303_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=IbM5MiKVETQ:y735mNWfej4:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn16@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-04-402_9ed8b046593bd03f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=IbM5MiKVETQ:y735mNWfej4:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn25@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-10-807_e2de3fbcbb8ea893.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-06-748_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=IbM5MiKVETQ:y735mNWfej4:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn98@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-07-329_9d567957b120a5a6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/IbM5MiKVETQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn2@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-10-767_143befabbd1283e9.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617605114819},{"createdTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"The death of the American mall was a warning sign that our dystopian future was closer than we all thought","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/retail-apocalypse-helped-spark-a-rapid-descent-into-dystopia-2021-3","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6064bceedaf0f10018f99488?format=jpeg\" alt=\"sears vaccination\" height=\"1630\" width=\"2174\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Sears has been turned into a COVID-19 vaccination center, aiming to vaccinate around 700 people a day.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Paul Hennessy/SOPA Images/LightRocket via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Americans getting vaccinated in bankrupt, empty malls paint a grim picture for life after COVID-19.</li>\n<li>Retail vacancy rates are at a 7-year high after decades of closures due to the rise of e-commerce.</li>\n<li>Brands are bailing out failing US policies, from healthcare to infrastructure - and it&#39;s only going to get worse.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As vaccines roll out across American, thousands of people aren&#39;t getting vaccinated at CVS pharmacies or local health clinics. Instead, they&#39;re heading to abandoned Kmarts, Sears, and <a href=\"https://www.wjol.com/toys-r-us-joliet-to-become-mass-vaccination-site/\">Toys R Us stores</a> to get their shots. </p><p>For American companies that have seen store counts collapse in recent years, the symbolism of having abandoned stores turned into mass vaccination clinics highlights how quickly the world was changing before the pandemic, and how COVID-19 accelerated a shift to an unfamiliar and sometimes dystopian future. </p><p>The end of the COVID-19 pandemic might be in sight as vaccine shots ramp up, but crumbling malls, the country&#39;s haphazard approach to healthcare, and brands looking to capitalize on the &#34;new normal&#34; suggest our new dystopian reality is here to stay.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6064bd82daf0f10018f9948d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"sears vaccine\" height=\"1428\" width=\"1904\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Townsquare Mall in Rockaway, New Jersey turned a former Sears into a vaccine &#34;mega&#34; site.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kena Betancur / AFP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>American malls are dying a slow and painful death</h2><p>The last decade has seen American cultural touchstones disintegrate as part of the retail apocalypse. </p><p>Companies like Sears and JCPenney spent over 100 years building their brands into household names - but <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/retail-apocalypse-last-decade-timeline-2019-12\">it took only 10 years</a> for an apocalypse to sweep through the retail industry, leaving vacant stores and dead malls in its wake.</p><p>The demise, like so much in the last decade, can be linked to the financial crisis: After the housing bubble burst in the late aughts, many <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/retail-apocalypse-last-decade-timeline-2019-12\">retailers were never quite able to get back on their feet</a>. Hundreds of thousands of employees were out of work, and private equity stepped in, burdening mall brands with <a href=\"https://newrepublic.com/article/145813/cause-consequences-retail-apocalypse\">massive amounts of debt</a>.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/1000-taco-bell-bellhops-coming-to-drive-thru-lanes-as-ch[â¦]weaks-restaurant-designs-for-a-post-pandemic-world-2021-3\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Taco Bell is adding 1,000 drive-thru &#39;bellhops&#39; as chain tweaks traditional and Cantina stores for a post pandemic world</a></em></p><p>The American mall began to face &#34;a death spiral,&#34; John M. Clapp, a professor at the University of Connecticut&#39;s Center for Real Estate, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-tsunami-of-store-closures-is-doubling-in-size-2017-6\">told Insider in 2017</a>.</p><p>&#34;Once a department store goes vacant that tends to be contagious because all those middle-mall stores - the nail salons and the jewelry stores - they are all depending on the traffic coming from the bigger retail stores,&#34; he said.</p><p>A report from Coresight Research <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/08/27/25percent-of-us-malls-are-set-to-shut-within-5-years-what-comes-next.html\">cited by CNBC</a> last August estimated that out of roughly 1,000 American malls, a quarter will close down in the next three to five years.</p><p>And, of course, it&#39;s impossible to ignore the Amazon effect: The Seattle bookseller sparked an e-commerce boom, leading to a race to the top for Amazon and its main competition, Walmart, and opening the direct-to-consumer floodgates. Companies like Glossier, Allbirds, and Casper led the way, eschewing a traditional retail experience in favor of online-only shopping. (Of course, all of those brands eventually opened <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/casper-dreamery-nap-room-nyc-review-photos-2018-7\">retail experiences</a> of their own.)</p><p>In what is perhaps the cruelest twist of irony, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-looks-to-turn-malls-into-giant-fulfillment-centers-report-2020-8\">Amazon reportedly held talks with Simon Property Group</a>, the biggest mall-owner in the US, to discuss converting empty retail space into fulfillment centers that pack and ship Amazon orders.</p><p>The pandemic has only made matters worse. Retail vacancy rates are <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/andriacheng/2021/01/13/us-2021-retail-vacancy-rate-may-rise-to-7-year-high-after-record-store-closings/?sh=6ef6d37468e8\">nearing a seven-year high,</a> after major chains announced closures of more than 12,000 stores in 2020. <a href=\"https://www.moodysanalytics.com/-/media/whitepaper/2020/ma-reis_covid-19_and_repurposing_retail_to_industrial_2020-08-27.pdf\">Moody&#39;s Analytics projects</a> that roughly 135 million square feet of vacant space may become available in regional malls nationwide within the next five years. These vacancies have left malls abandoned, and they readily turned into vaccination sites.</p><p>Many laid off retail workers have either <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/recode/21717536/department-store-middle-class-amazon-online-shopping-covid-19\">pivoted</a> to discount chains that pay employees significantly less, or Amazon itself. And though Amazon pays workers $15 an hour, warehouse jobs are more physically demanding and delivery drivers said they&#39;ve <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-drivers-say-peeing-in-bottles-common-despite-company-denials-2021-3\">dehydrated themselves</a> to get through a shift without bathroom breaks.</p><p>In lieu of an adequate government safety net to ensure Americans get fair pay and health care even as businesses shutter, brands are - unfortunately - left to pick up the pieces.</p><h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60662cd352f11d0019431aec?format=jpeg\" alt=\"COVID Vaccine Line\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>People wait in line in a Disneyland parking lot to receive COVID-19 vaccines.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Valerie Macon/AFP/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></h2><h2>Things are only going to get weirder </h2><p>The complete disruption of the pandemic puts Americans in a position where the &#34;new normal&#34; is a flexible term. As seen by the transformation of malls into vaccination sites, something that would seem straight out of &#34;28 Days Later&#34; in 2019 can be completely acceptable in 2021. </p><p>The factors that allowed for this cobbled together solution - a broken retail system saving a healthcare system stretched to the breaking point - are not going away.</p><p>The inclination to turn to companies to fix broken infrastructure can run the gambit from creative at best to disturbing at worst. For example: </p><ul><li>Domino&#39;s announced a campaign to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominos-pothole-repair-raises-questions-2018-6\">fill potholes in 2018,</a> allowing customers to nominate their towns for repairs.</li><li>Light-beer legend Natural Light has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/natty-light-donate-10-million-student-loan-debt-2019-1\">spent millions of dollars paying off fans&#39; student loans.</a></li><li>Companies like Gap, Target, and Warby Parker helped staff the nation&#39;s polls on Election Day by corralling <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/companies-recruit-350-000-poll-workers-for-u-s-election-11599384600\">hundreds of thousands of employees</a> to serve as poll workers</li><li>A Chick-fil-A manager in South Carolina had to step in to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chick-fil-a-manager-rescues-drive-thru-covid-19-vaccine-clinic-2021-1\">direct his town&#39;s drive-thru COVID-19 vaccine site</a> after it was hamstrung by computer issues.</li></ul><p>And as state governments work to vaccinate their citizens as quickly and efficiently as possible, they&#39;ve turned to other capitalist symbols of the before-times to help carry out their plans.</p><p>Beginning in January, lines snaked around the parking lot at Disneyland, but not to visit Thunder Mountain or the Haunted Mansion - the theme park, shuttered since March 2020, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/disneyland-administered-100000-covid-vaccines-2021-2\">became a &#34;super&#34; vaccination site</a> where hundreds of thousands of doses have been administered.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biggest-obstacles-23andme-faces-in-going-public-s4-analysis-2021-3\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">We just got the best look yet at the consumer genetics market ahead of 23andMe&#39;s public debut. Here are the 5 biggest obstacles the $3.6 billion company will have to overcome.</a></em></p><p>Major league sports stadiums, many of which sat empty and dark for most of last year, have also become <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HITMM4_nVxY\">mass vaccination sites</a>. Where fans would have once lined up to get let into a football or baseball game, they&#39;re now lining up to get a COVID shot. </p><p>Brands have been bailing out the US health system throughout the pandemic. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coors-beer-company-makes-hand-sanitizer-amid-coronavirus-pandemic-2020-3\">Coors beer</a> breweries transformed into hand sanitizer manufacturers. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/volkswagen-faurecia-donate-thousands-gowns-masks-new-york-city-hospitals-2020-4\">Volkswagen</a> made hospital equipment after the country&#39;s gown and mask shortage got so bad nurses resorted to wearing trash bags.</p><p>This kind of corporate contingency plan shows no sign of stopping after the pandemic subsides - in fact, it may even be coming for schools next. <a href=\"https://www.sevendaysvt.com/OffMessage/archives/2021/03/03/burlington-high-school-opens-downtown-campus-in-former-macys\">A mall in Vermont became a safe-haven for a high school</a> after the school, just before it was set to reopen for in-person learning, was found to have elevated levels of toxic chemicals known to cause cancer.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60677d6d856cd700198a2fe6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"AP21084746481358 (1)\" height=\"2978\" width=\"3971\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Downtown Burlington High School.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Downtown Burlington High School.</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>There may, however, be a more nefarious side to some companies lending a hand, even during the COVID-19 pandemic. CVS and Walgreens - which have collectively given nearly 20 million shots so far - are <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/cvs-walgreens-look-for-big-data-reward-from-covid-19-vaccinations-11614681180\">reportedly looking to cash in on data collected from people they administer vaccines to</a>. And drug companies that made the COVID-19 vaccines <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/vaccine-patents-ips-monopoly-vaccination-process-us-biden-africa-2021-2\">won&#39;t give up their patents</a> to help vaccinate the rest of the world.</p><p>These self-serving tactics should be taken as a warning sign as the US increasingly relies on brands to build a post-pandemic future. In some cases, companies have unique insight into problems - such as a Chick-fil-A manager helping with a vaccine drive-thru. But, relying too fully on corporations whose ultimate focus is their bottom line is not just dystopian, it&#39;s dangerous. </p><p>The pandemic has shown just how quickly things can change. As the country rebuilds, it needs to be on solid ground, instead of relying on the magnanimity of brands.<strong><br></strong></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"Chinese troops are heading to Russia to take part in a tough mountain-warfare competition for the first src=\"https://i.insider.com/5eeb7e3d3ad8617291295024?format=jpeg\" alt=\"China Chinese troops soldiers Tibet training\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chinese soldiers train on a snowy plateau in Tibet, June 11, 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\">TPG/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A team of Chinese soldiers is heading to Russia for gruelling winter-warfare exercises.</li>\n<li>The Chinese soldiers will be learning from Russian military practice in extreme conditions.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>China is sending a group of soldiers to take part in a military competition in <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/topics/china-russia-relations\" data-v-2a60e86e=\"\">Russia</a> that will test their winter skills in gruelling mountain conditions.</p><p>According to China&#39;s defence ministry, 11 soldiers from the Harbin-based 78th Group Army unit under Northern Theatre Command will travel to Russia on April 2 to take part in a 50 km (31-mile) trek through the Western Sayan mountain range.</p><p>Challenges will include locating someone caught in an avalanche, fixed-rope descent and rescue, as well as shooting and grenade exercises.</p><p>The Sayan March competition, from April 14-17, is the first of 34 exercises taking place within the framework of this year&#39;s International Army Games. It is the first time China has taken part in this preliminary stage of the competition.</p><p>Team leader Cui Yingbin told military newspaper The PLA Daily that China aimed to check its level of combat readiness through the games.</p><p>&#34;By competing on the same stage with servicemen from various countries, we can not only further test the level of our military&#39;s combat readiness, but also enhance mutual friendship and deepen military exchanges and cooperation between countries.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f0c9e302618b91ec344d169?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chinese China army soldiers Xinjiang\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chinese soldiers patrol the border of Khunjerab Pass in Kashgar in China&#39;s western Xinjiang region, November 21, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">STR/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The report also quoted Xu Bing, one of the 11 selected soldiers, who said all the Chinese participants were determined to perform well in the competition.</p><p>China has a tradition of turning to Russia in developing its military prowess, from hardware design to the structure of its armed forces. The Sayan March competition is an opportunity to learn more about Russian practices in extreme conditions, according to Hong Kong based military analyst Song Zhongping.</p><p>&#34;China has to deal with its border dispute with India, and the battlefield in the Tibetan plateau has extremely cold weather and high altitude. China needs to gain experience to tackle new tensions and prepare its response to provocations from India too,&#34; said Song, a former PLA instructor.</p><p>&#34;What&#39;s more, the Chinese military&#39;s missions have expanded from safeguarding its national interests to protecting overseas interests as well, which would cover places with rough conditions and extreme weather.&#34;</p><p>India and China share one of the world&#39;s longest land borders and there have been several bloody conflicts, including the 1962 Himalayan war. Skirmishes have continued to break out sporadically over the years. <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3122320/china-india-border-clash-june-left-four-chinese-dead-one\" data-v-2a60e86e=\"\">Four Chinese and 20 Indian soldiers died in June 2020</a>, in the deadliest clash in decades.</p><p>Beijing has also improved cooperation with Russia - especially on the military front - whenever China has faced setbacks in its relations with the major Western democracies. In December, the two countries signed a 10-year extension to their agreement on mutual launch notifications of ballistic missiles and space rockets.</p><p>China also took part last year in Russia&#39;s International Army Games, as well as the Kavkaz-2020 large scale military exercise. The two countries held their second joint aerial strategic patrol in the Sea of Japan and the East China Sea in December. Their first joint patrol of the area took place in July 2019.</p><p>This year marks the 20th anniversary of the Treaty of Good-Neighbourliness and Friendly Cooperation between the two countries.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/chinese-troops-head-to-russia-for-tough-mountain-warfare-competition-2021-4'>Business MyPillow&#39;s products have been pulled by at least 22 retailers, including <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/where-to-buy-mypillow-and-what-companies-cut-ties-2021-1#kohls-cited-decreased-customer-demand-as-the-reason-it-will-not-reorder-from-my-pillow-2\">Sam&#39;s voter-fraud conspiracy theories</a>.</p><p>Lindell spoke to Insider in a phone interview Thursday, where he discussed the approximately $65 million in lost revenue this year that this is expected to cost the company, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mypillow-ceo-mike-lindell-dominion-lawsuit-losing-money-2021-2\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"4276047653640e209d1b89ac22f8585a\">as previously reported by</a> Insider&#39;s Jacob Shamsian.</p><p>&#34;We obviously can&#39;t get that back, we&#39;re going to lose that,&#34; Lindell told Insider on Thursday. </p><p>But the growing audience for radio and podcast shows could help MyPillow fill this gap through direct-to-consumer (DTC) sales by creating more advertising opportunities, he said.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;re going to look at other strategies to try and get that revenue back,&#34; Lindell said. &#34;We&#39;re looking at every space for that.&#34;</p><p>&#34;We&#39;ve expanded so much in radio and podcast, that&#39;s our biggest expansion right now,&#34; he added. &#34;It&#39;s just booming right now. We hope that that makes up a lot of it.&#34;</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/my-pillow-ceo-mike-lindell-trump-final-days-2021-1?inline-read-more\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"608f463ab846e913813f6154719accb4\">The MyPillow guy says God helped him beat a crack addiction to build a multimillion-dollar empire. Now his religious devotion to Trump threatens to bring it all crashing down.</a></em></p><p>In court filings, the company has said that it spends around $5 million a month on advertising, per <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/01/27/business/mike-lindell-mypillow.html\">The New York Times</a>.</p><p>Because MyPillow has always focused on direct consumer advertising, the shift from retailers to DTC sales won&#39;t be hard for the brand, Matt Voda, CEO of OptiMine, told Insider. </p><p>Lindell said in late March that lots of customers have been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mypillow-mike-lindell-minnesota-home-trump-dominion-lawsuit-safety-2021-3\">buying products directly through MyPillow</a>, and that it&#39;s had to hire more staff to meet demand. It&#39;s expanded beyond just pillows, and Lindell told Insider Thursday it had more than 110 different products.</p><p>&#34;TV traditionally helps box store sales, but I&#39;m very confident that the radio and podcasts are gonna make up a lot of the lost box store revenue and retailers,&#34; Lindell said.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mypillow-mike-lindell-infomercials-advertising-marketing-brand-tv-2021-3\">Lindell told Insider</a> that during the pandemic more people were watching TV so the company&#39;s infomercials can reach a bigger audience than they could in the past, but that as the US opens up MyPillow will pivot to spend more money on digital advertising.</p><p>Analysts told Insider that infomercials have worked well for the brand in the past - but it <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mypillow-mike-lindell-infomercials-advertising-marketing-brand-tv-2021-3\">may need to knuckle down on social-media advertising if it wants to attract new customers</a>.</p><p>MyPillow is a private company, so its financial information isn&#39;t published, but he told The New York Times that its 2019 revenues <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/01/27/business/mike-lindell-mypillow.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"18621cdd7b3898955486c17946ccc17b\">topped $300 million</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/mike-lindell-mypillow-infomercials-revenue-retailers-radio-podcast-sales-profit-2021-4'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a </a></p><p>The tweet in question was posted in 2018. <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/998454539941367808\">Musk wrote:</a> &#34;Nothing stopping Tesla team at our car plant from voting union. Could do so tmrw if they wanted. But why pay union dues &#38; give up stock options for nothing? Our safety record is 2X better than when plant was UAW &#38; everybody already gets healthcare.&#34; </p><p>Last month, the NLRB ordered Musk to remove the tweet and publicly address the unlawful tweet at all of its sites, and include speech that says, &#34;WE WILL take appropriate steps to ensure Musk complies with our directive,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-tesla-nrlb-musk-idUSKBN2BQ0JU\">according to Reuters.</a></p><p>The NLRB told Tesla to reinstate a former employee and revoke a ban on the sharing of union details in its car park without prior company permission.</p><p>Tesla workers at its Fremont plant had been trying to <a pandemic, despite previously telling staff they were able to do so. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"3 things you might not know about the vaunted F-15 fighter jet","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/things-you-might-not-know-about-the-f15-fighter-jet-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa99075f7d1cb0019e3a968?format=jpeg\" alt=\"f 15\" height=\"1050\" width=\"2100\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Air Force F-15C Eagles over the island of Okinawa during a solar eclipse.\n<p class=\"copyright\">USAF/Airman 1st Class Chad Warren</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The F-15 has been a workhorse for the US Air Force for more than 40 years.</li>\n<li>Newer, more sophisticated jets have joined the service in that time, but the F-15 has a few features that keep it in high demand.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The Mcdonnell Douglas F-15 Eagle and its subsequent variants have served as <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2tLrC4o\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">America&#39;s</a> workhorse intercept fighters for over 40 years.</p><p>For a short time, it seemed as though the F-15 would fade into history as it was being replaced by its stealthy successor, the F-22 Raptor. But the F-22 program ended and its supply chain was cannibalized to support F-35 production.</p><p><a href=\"https://amzn.to/2tLrC4o\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">America&#39;s</a> relatively small fleet of fifth generation air superiority fighters isn&#39;t large enough to replace the venerable F-15. Instead, Uncle Sam has agreed to <a href=\"https://sofrep.com/news/americas-fighter-of-the-future-is-the-f-15-air-force-wants-to-order-a-dozen-new-f-15x-fighters-in-2020/\">purchase <em>more</em></a> fourth generation F-15s to replace those quickly aging out of service.</p><p>So what is it about the F-15 that&#39;s so special that <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2uL6rA9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">America&#39;s Air Force</a> can&#39;t seem to get enough of them? Quite a bit, actually.</p><h2>It&#39;s the fastest fighter jet in America&#39;s arsenal</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/52ea8b7f6bb3f76e25631ee5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"f-15 eagle afghanistan\" height=\"3456\" width=\"5184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.dvidshub.net/search/?q=f-15&#43;eagle&#43;sunset&#38;filter%5Btype%5D=image&#38;page=32#.UuqLWbvLicw\" target=\"_blank\">US Air Force</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Although the F-35 Joint Strike Fighter tends to garner most of the headlines, the F-15Cs and F-15Ds currently run by the <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2uL6rA9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">US Air Force</a> actually beat out the F-35 in a handful of crucial air-combat metrics.</p><p>The F-35, it&#39;s important to note, wasn&#39;t designed to serve as a dedicated dog fighter: It was built to engage ground targets primarily. The <a href=\"https://sofrep.com/fightersweep/what-exactly-was-the-f-15-active-aircraft/\">F-15</a>, on the other hand, was designed from the ground up to go toe to toe with the best Soviet fighters in the sky - and back then Russian fighters were really something to be feared.</p><p>The F-15&#39;s top speed, of slightly over Mach 2.4 or 1,875 mph, is the subject of a bit of debate, as many claim the powerful fighter can go even faster. Either way, it leaves platforms like the F-35 - with a top speed of just 1,230 mph or so - in its dust.</p><p>Even the top-of-the-line F-22 can only achieve Mach 2.2. This gives the F-15 the crown of <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2tLrC4o\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">America&#39;s</a> fastest fighter jet.</p><h2>It&#39;s got serious range</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cd9a23e021b4c25e83ab503?format=jpeg\" alt=\"F-15C Eagle refueling during deterrence patrol\" height=\"2804\" width=\"4986\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A F-15C Eagle during aerial refueling.\n<p class=\"copyright\">U.S. Air Force photo by Senior Airman Keifer Bowes</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>While the US Navy struggles to find ways to increase the operational range of its carrier-based F/A-18 Super Hornets and F-35C Joint Strike Fighters to stretch carrier ops further away from Chinese anti-ship ship missiles, the <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2uL6rA9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">Air Force&#39;s</a> F-15s are boasting around <em>three times</em> the range of their Navy peers when flying with their three external fuel tanks.</p><p>In total, the F-15 can <a href=\"https://militarymachine.com/f-15-facts/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">cover</a> around 3,000 nautical miles without needing to refuel. Thanks to its inflight refueling capabilities, it could feasibly even stay airborne and in the fight for as long as the <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2t2Qchr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">pilot</a>, and its ordnance, last.</p><h2>It&#39;s got a perfect combat record</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ad7b7a0cd862434008b47ab?format=jpeg\" alt=\"US Air Force F-15 Eagle\" height=\"912\" width=\"1400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An F-15 Eagle fires an AIM-7 Sparrow medium range air-to-air missile.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force/Master Sgt. Michael Ammons</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Despite being in operation for over four decades and <a href=\"https://www.boeing.com/defense/f-15/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">serving</a> in the <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2uL6rA9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">air forces</a> of not just the United States, but also Japan, Israel, South Korea, Saudi Arabia, Singapore and Qatar, no F-15 has ever been shot down by an opposing force.</p><p>Unlike the F-35 and F-22, which rely on stealth to avoid detection and therefore, engagement, the F-15 has never been sneaky.</p><p>Without stealth to protect the aircraft from opposing fighters or ground-based air defenses, F-15 <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2t2Qchr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">pilots</a> have had to rely on tactics, skill and speed to outmaneuver or entirely avoid enemy contact.</p><p><em>This article was originally published on January 2, 2020.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/things-you-might-not-know-about-the-f15-fighter-jet-2021-4'>Business
