reasons to be skeptical about warnings of a near-term or even medium-term invasion of Taiwan by Beijing.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The top US military commander for the Asia-Pacific region, Adm. Philip Davidson, raised eyebrows at a recent Senate hearing when <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/mar/10/china-could-invade-taiwan-in-next-six-years-top-us-admiral-warns\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">he suggested China could invade Taiwan within the next six years</a>.</p><p>The nominee to replace Davidson at the head of US Indo-Pacific Command, Adm. John Aquilino, then went a step further, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/mar/23/taiwan-china-threat-admiral-john-aquilino\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">telling the same committee last week that in his view</a>, &#34;This problem is much closer to us than most think and we have to take this on.&#34;</p><p>At first glance, such concerns might seem justified. The Chinese Communist Party has always viewed the annexation of Taiwan as a key strategic goal, but its posture toward the democratic, self-ruling island has grown markedly more belligerent in recent years. Chinese leaders have publicly reiterated their willingness to use force to &#34;unify&#34; Taiwan with the mainland, while ramping up the pace of military activities in and around the Taiwan Strait.</p><p>Meanwhile, President Xi Jinping has presided over the rapid growth and modernization of the People&#39;s Liberation Army-particularly its navy, air force and missile arsenal. Where Taipei once enjoyed certain advantages in the event of a military conflict, including technological superiority and the benefits of island defense, many military analysts now conclude that China could take Taiwan by force, and that the <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/national-security/china-s-growing-firepower-casts-doubt-whether-u-s-could-n1262148\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">United States would be hard-pressed to stop it</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f501e89e6ff30001d4e6c54?format=jpeg\" alt=\"China amphibious tanks invasion\" height=\"1694\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chinese People&#39;s Liberation Army amphibious tanks land on a beach during a Sino-Russian military exercise near the Shandong Peninsula, China, August 24, 2005.\n<p class=\"copyright\">China Photos/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Nonetheless, there are many good reasons to cast a gimlet eye on Davidson and Aquilino&#39;s warnings of a near-term or even medium-term Chinese invasion of Taiwan.</p><p>First, the US military brass has a long history of inflating threats in order to ensure continued support from elected officials, particularly the lawmakers who fund their operations. It should be no more surprising that the head of Indo-Pacific Command is hyping the prospect of Chinese military adventurism than it is to hear the head of Southern Command opining that fragile states in the Western Hemisphere pose an <a href=\"https://foreignpolicy.com/2015/08/04/the-existential-angst-of-americas-top-generals-threat-inflation-islamic-state/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">&#34;existential&#34; threat to the United States</a>.</p><p>The Pentagon&#39;s own annual report to Congress on Chinese military capabilities, released last year, makes clear that an amphibious invasion of Taiwan would be &#34;<a href=\"https://www.defense.gov/Newsroom/Releases/Release/Article/2332126/dod-releases-2020-report-on-military-and-security-developments-involving-the-pe/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a significant political and military risk</a>&#34; for China.</p><p>Large-scale amphibious invasions are hard to pull off under the best of circumstances, and this would likely be the largest mass military mobilization the world has seen since D-Day. It would require the PLA to transport its soldiers across a body of water nearly five times as wide as the English Channel, all while ensuring that it maintains unchallenged control of the seas and airspace around the island.</p><p>As Taiwan-based writer Brian Hioe recently pointed out in a <a href=\"https://newbloommag.net/2021/03/29/china-invasion-possibility/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">piece for the online magazine New Bloom</a>, it is doubtful that the PLA currently has adequate amphibious lift capability to sustain an invasion and occupation of Taiwan.</p><p>China could try to make up for this deficiency by utilizing coast guard ships, commercial vessels and even fishing boats - engineering what <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/05/china/china-world-biggest-navy-intl-hnk-ml-dst/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">some analysts have called a &#34;reverse Dunkirk&#34;</a> - but that would entail its own discrete risks.</p><p>Whatever the case, it seems clear that Chinese military planners would prefer to have more time to develop their amphibious capabilities before attempting to take Taiwan by force.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f501e897ed0ee001e25d28b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Taiwan China amphibious landing military exercise\" height=\"1634\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Taiwan&#39;s military holds a large-scale exercise in the southern part of the island simulating an attempted amphibious landing by Chinese forces, May 30, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kyodo News Stills via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Beijing must also factor in the likelihood of an intervention from the US and its allies, particularly Japan, which hosts the largest overseas contingent of American active-duty military personnel. Most of them are stationed in Okinawa, just 750 kilometers - roughly 466 miles - from Taiwan.</p><p>In recent years, the already robust bipartisan consensus on Capitol Hill in favor of supporting Taiwan&#39;s autonomy from Beijing has only strengthened, and US public opinion polls also <a href=\"https://thediplomat.com/2020/10/poll-shows-increase-in-american-support-for-defending-taiwan/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">indicate growing support for the defense of Taiwan</a>.</p><p>Japan, too, maintains close unofficial ties with Taiwan, and would view any Chinese aggression toward the island as a threat to its own security. <a href=\"https://asia.nikkei.com/Politics/International-relations/Biden-s-Asia-policy/Biden-and-Suga-to-note-Taiwan-Strait-in-April-joint-statement\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">According to a recent report in the Nikkei</a>, a leading Japanese newspaper, Prime Minister Suga Yoshihide and President Joe Biden are planning to underscore the importance of stability in the Taiwan Strait in their joint statement when they meet in Washington later this month.</p><p>As the Nikkei notes, the last time Japanese and American leaders expressed such concern was in 1969. Should it wish to forcibly annex Taiwan, Beijing would have to accept the high likelihood of a war with its top two trading partners.</p><p>Even if China successfully pulls off a cross-strait invasion while keeping the US and its allies at bay, the human and economic toll would be nothing short of catastrophic. Taiwan&#39;s technology and manufacturing sectors play crucial roles in global supply chains, and Beijing would likely come under tremendous international pressure, including economic sanctions, to reverse course.</p><p>Bonnie Glaser and Matthew Funaiole, two scholars at the Center for Strategic and International Studies, have also argued that China would have to deal with the prospect of a prolonged resistance movement on the island.</p><p>&#34;An all-out invasion of Taiwan might bog down the PLA in a counterinsurgency effort that lasts for years, which could compromise the military&#39;s modernization efforts, drain precious resources from the Chinese economy, and lead to dissatisfaction at home as the body bags come home, many of them likely to be their parents&#39; only sons,&#34; <a href=\"https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/05/15/chinas-provocations-around-taiwan-arent-a-crisis/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">they wrote in Foreign Policy last year</a>.</p><p>This would be exactly the type of aggressive military intervention and occupation that China has castigated the US for mounting in the past.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d405e2d100a2442da30650c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chinese marines navy landing craft beach\" height=\"957\" width=\"1400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chinese troops board landing craft during an amphibious exercise on the coast of southeast China&#39;s Fujian Province, November 27, 1995.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>None of this means that China&#39;s threatening behavior against Taiwan should not be taken seriously.</p><p>PLA warplanes have intruded into Taiwan&#39;s air defense identification zone with such frequency in recent months that the Taiwanese military has <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-taiwan-security/taiwan-says-tracks-intruding-chinese-aircraft-with-missiles-not-always-scrambling-idUSKBN2BL0JS\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">decided to stop scrambling fighter jets upon each incursion</a>, opting to track them with ground-based missiles in order to conserve resources.</p><p>Deputy Defense Minister Chang Che-ping told lawmakers in Taipei this week that he considered China&#39;s provocations to be a kind of &#34;war of attrition,&#34; likely referring to the fact that Taiwan has incurred hundreds of millions of dollars in additional maintenance costs to facilitate the frequent scrambling of its jets, many of which are older models.</p><p>Chang&#39;s comments speak to a core pillar of China&#39;s strategy: Wearing Taiwan down psychologically in the hope that, eventually, its leaders will be forced to negotiate the terms of their surrender.</p><p>Of course, Beijing itself has undermined that strategy with its brutal crackdown on pro-democracy figures in Hong Kong and on the city&#39;s autonomy, making a mockery of the &#34;One Country, Two Systems&#34; approach that Chinese leaders once put forward as a template for unification with Taiwan.</p><p>Going forward, China is more likely to continue and perhaps build upon its multipronged pressure campaign against Taiwan. This could mean further efforts to isolate Taipei on the world stage by trying to poach its remaining diplomatic allies and continuing to block its access to international organizations.</p><p>It could even try to test Taiwan&#39;s resolve - and the international community&#39;s commitment to defending it - by taking over one of the <a href=\"https://www.worldpoliticsreview.com/articles/29494/a-small-island-chain-could-be-the-next-flashpoint-in-taiwan-china-relations\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">smaller islands that Taiwan administers in the South China Sea</a>. But at least in the immediate term, it is difficult to envision Chinese leaders justifying the political, economic and reputational costs of a full-scale invasion of Taiwan.</p><p>Pentagon officials are fond of saying that the US military is a planning organization. Its job is to plan for contingencies, and a military conflict over Taiwan is certainly worth putting at or near the top of the list. There are a number of scenarios that, while improbable, could spark an escalatory cycle and change China&#39;s cost-to-benefit calculus with regard to Taiwan.</p><p>But no one is served by publicly exaggerating the likelihood of conflict in the Taiwan Strait - not the United States and certainly not the people of Taiwan, who ultimately have the most at stake.</p><p><em>Elliot Waldman is the senior editor of World Politics Review.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"The two final crew members who will orbit Earth on a SpaceX ship, as part of the all-civilian Inspiration4Â mission, have been revealed","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-final-members-of-the-all-civilian-inspiration4mission-revealed-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6065e47b902281001950a91c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Inspiration4_Crew_at_Launch_Site\" height=\"1500\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Inspiration4 Crew at historic Launchpad 39A, provided by SpaceX. Chris Sembroski, Hayley Arceneaux, Sian Proctor and Jared Isaacman.\n<p class=\"copyright\">SpaceX/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The final two crew members have been announced for Inspiration4&#39;s civilian mission to orbit Earth. </li>\n<li>Dr. Sian Proctor and Chris Sembroski have been named as additional crew members on SpaceX&#39;s ship.</li>\n<li>They will be joining Jared Isaacman and Hayley Arceneaux on the mission in September.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>In <a href=\"https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20210330005265/en/Final-Crew-Members-Named-for-World%E2%80%99s-First-All-Civilian-Mission-to-Space\">an announcement</a> earlier this week, SpaceX&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-inspiration4-first-ever-private-astronaut-mission-in-late-2021-2021-2\">Inspiration4</a>, the world&#39;s first all-civilian rocket ride to orbit Earth, revealed the final two members of the four-person crew that will undergo a historic journey into space.</p><p>Chris Sembroski and Dr. Sian Proctor were the additional two people who won seats on SpaceX&#39;s Dragon spaceship.</p><p>They will accompany <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com.au/spacex-inspiration4-first-ever-private-astronaut-mission-in-late021-2-2021-2\">Jared Isaacman</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.in/tech/news/a-29-year-old-woman-who-survived-cancer-as-a-child-was-just-selected-to-fly-to-space-aboard-spacexs-rocket/articleshow/81157380.cms\">Hayley Arceneaux</a> on the mission, where all four will ride aboard the Dragon spacecraft to be launched into orbit by SpaceX&#39;s Falcon 9 rocket. </p><p>SpaceX is planning for a liftoff of no earlier than September 15. The ship will depart from Kennedy Space Center&#39;s Launch Complex 39A.</p><p>It is expected to orbit Earth for three days at an altitude of approximately 335 miles, where the crew will eventually touch down off the coast of Florida for retrieval. </p><h2><strong>Here&#39;s what we know about the four crew members</strong></h2><h3><strong>Jared Isaacman </strong></h3><p>Entrepreneur and philanthropist, Isaacman is a 38-year-old tech billionaire, pilot, and chief executive of Shift4 Payments, a Pennsylvania-based payment processing company. He will charter the flight.</p><p>Though he said he has spent more than 6,000 hours flying jets and ex-military aircraft, he has never been to space. Neither have his three fellow passengers, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-inspiration4-first-ever-private-astronaut-mission-in-late-2021-2021-2\">as Insider previously reported.</a></p><p>Isaacman had several goals in planning this mission: to give a diverse community of individuals the opportunity to fly into space and raise money for St. Jude Children&#39;s Research Hospital in Memphis. </p><p>&#34;The stars really aligned for us in terms of this group&#34;, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/30/science/30spacex-inspiration4.html?surface=intl-hp-in-other-news&fellback=false&req_id=799563277&algo=bandit-all-surfaces-geo-intl_diversified_impression_cut_iion_2&variant=2_bandit-all-surfaces-geo-intl_impression_cut_2&imp_id=648016376&action=click&module=&pgtype=Homepage&#38;module=&#38;pgtype=Homepage\">he told The New York Times.</a></p><p>&#34;We promised the crew representing some of the best of humanitarian qualities exemplifying our mission ideals of leadership, hope, prosperity and generosity. And I&#39;m pleased to report that we&#39;ve accomplished that goal,&#34; he said. </p><p>Isaacman will serve as the commander for the SpaceX mission. </p><h3><strong>Hayley Arceneaux </strong></h3><p>Announced earlier in February, a 29-year-old childhood cancer survivor and physician assistant at St. Jude Children&#39;s Research, Arceneaux is the second civilian to join the crew.</p><p>At the age of 10, Arceneaux had part of her femur removed from bone cancer. There are many sporting activities that she cannot do for fear of risking an uncontrolled fall. This is because of a metal rod in her left leg, which was implanted during her bone-cancer treatments as a child.</p><p>But now she has the chance to set herself free from all limitations. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.in/tech/news/a-29-year-old-woman-who-survived-cancer-as-a-child-was-just-selected-to-fly-to-space-aboard-spacexs-rocket/articleshow/81157380.cms\">In an interview with Insider</a>, she said her orthopedic surgeon told her: &#34;There&#39;s going to be no limits on you in space.&#34;</p><p>Arceneaux will be the youngest American to fly into space and the first with a prosthetic body part. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6065ec7f52f11d0019431979?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Eo6X0V5U0AEXm2x\" height=\"2730\" width=\"3640\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SpaceX&#39;s Starship SN8 flight test in December 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">SpaceX/Twitter</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h3><strong>Sian Proctor </strong></h3><p>Proctor, a geoscientist, science communication specialist, and analog astronaut, is one of the newest crew members aboard SpaceX&#39;s Dragon spacecraft. </p><p>Proctor secured her seat after winning a contest sponsored by Isaacman&#39;s e-commerce company, <a href=\"https://www.today.com/news/inspiration4-team-1st-all-civilian-crew-going-space-revealed-today-t213378\">Today reported.</a></p><p>The contest required all entrants to design an online store using Shift4 Payments&#39; software and then tweet a video describing their space fantasies, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/30/science/30spacex-inspiration4.html?surface=intl-hp-in-other-news&fellback=false&req_id=799563277&algo=bandit-all-surfaces-geo-intl_diversified_impression_cut_iion_2&variant=2_bandit-all-surfaces-geo-intl_impression_cut_2&imp_id=648016376&action=click&module=&pgtype=Homepage&#38;module=&#38;pgtype=Homepage\">per The New York Times.</a></p><p><a href=\"https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20210330005265/en/Final-Crew-Members-Named-for-World%E2%80%99s-First-All-Civilian-Mission-to-Space\">Proctor told Business Wire</a>: &#34;This opportunity is proof that hard work and perseverance can pay off in unimaginable ways,&#34; said Dr. Proctor. &#34;I have always believed that I was preparing for something special, and that moment has arrived with Inspiration4. </p><p>Her excitement was palpable in an interview with Today&#39;s Tom Costello. &#34;It&#39;s like opening up the chocolate bar and seeing the golden ticket to Willy Wonka and the chocolate factory!&#34; she said. </p><h3><strong>Chris Sembroski </strong></h3><p>Joining the other three members is Sembroski, 41, a Lockheed Martin employee and Air Force veteran. </p><p>Sembroski was selected from nearly 72,000 entries in a contributing fundraising campaign for St. Jude. He will act as a mission specialist, aiding payloads and science experiments during the flight. </p><p>&#34;Joining the Inspiration4 crew and its mission of support for St. Jude is truly a dream come true. It is my hope that this flight will inspire others to pay that generosity forward by pledging their support for St. Jude and encouraging kids to dream the impossible, ushering in a new era of space exploration open to all,&#34; he said <a href=\"https://inspiration4.com/crew\">in a statement.</a></p><p>Sembroski first heard about the mission from an advertisement during this year&#39;s Super Bowl event.</p><p>&#34;That was just kind of intriguing,&#34; he told<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/30/science/30spacex-inspiration4.html?surface=intl-hp-in-other-news&fellback=false&req_id=799563277&algo=bandit-all-surfaces-geo-intl_diversified_impression_cut_iion_2&variant=2_bandit-all-surfaces-geo-intl_impression_cut_2&imp_id=648016376&action=click&module=&pgtype=Homepage&#38;module=&#38;pgtype=Homepage\"> The New York Times</a>. &#34;And so, it&#39;s like, &#39;All right, I&#39;ll donate to St. Jude and throw my name in the hat to see what happens.&#39;&#34;</p><p>The Inspiration4 crew will undergo commercial astronaut training by SpaceX. They will receive emergency preparedness training, as well as partial and full mission stimulations. </p><p>&#34;This is about mental toughness,&#34; Isaacman <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/30/science/30spacex-inspiration4.html?surface=intl-hp-in-other-news&fellback=false&req_id=799563277&algo=bandit-all-surfaces-geo-intl_diversified_impression_cut_iion_2&variant=2_bandit-all-surfaces-geo-intl_impression_cut_2&imp_id=648016376&action=click&module=&pgtype=Homepage&#38;module=&#38;pgtype=Homepage\">told The New York Times.</a> &#34;Getting uncomfortable, staying uncomfortable - and how well you perform when you are uncomfortable.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-final-members-of-the-all-civilian-inspiration4mission-revealed-2021-4'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=z7HkBlld20o:WWJt6eaQ2hg:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=z7HkBlld20o:WWJt6eaQ2hg:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=z7HkBlld20o:WWJt6eaQ2hg:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"The US has its own supply-chain crisis brewing as dozens of cargo ships remain stuck off the coast of LA as they wait to dock","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/cargo-ships-waiting-to-dock-california-contributes-supply-chain-crisis-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60674b42a7d803001963e7ba?format=jpeg\" alt=\"AP21072860197380\" height=\"2675\" width=\"3567\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Associated Press</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>28 ships were anchored off the coast of Los Angeles and Long Beach waiting to dock on Thursday.</li>\n<li>The California ports are congested and account for about one third of US imports.</li>\n<li>The port delays pile on a host of supply-chain issues.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>While the Suez Canal jam <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/suez-canal-reopened-supply-chain-issues-shipping-delays-experts-2021-3\">may have captured public attention before the cargo ship Ever Given was freed</a>, the US is quietly facing its own supply-chain crisis as dozens of freighters float off the coast of Los Angeles, waiting for dock space to open up.</p><p>California ports in Los Angeles and Long Beach account for about one third of US imports. These ports operate as a primary source of imports from China and have been heavily congested for months. </p><p>On Thursday, 28 ships were anchored off the coast waiting for a spot to open up to unload at Los Angeles and Long Beach ports, according to <a href=\"https://twitter.com/MXSOCAL?ref_src=twsrc%5Egoogle%7Ctwcamp%5Eserp%7Ctwgr%5Eauthor\">data</a> from the Marine Exchange of Southern California.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Marine Exchange  (@MXSOCAL) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1377832492317569025?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 2, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>The Southern California ports are facing more congestion than ever before, Kip Louttit, executive director of the Marine Exchange of Southern California, told <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/americas-imports-are-stuck-on-ships-floating-just-off-los-angeles-11617183002\">The Wall Street Journal. </a></p><p>&#34;Under normal conditions, container ships rarely anchor,&#34; Louttit said.</p><p>The ships carry millions of dollars worth of popular imports, including <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/suez-canal-reopened-supply-chain-issues-shipping-delays-experts-2021-3\">furniture</a>, auto parts, clothes, electronics, and plastics, according to <a href=\"https://www.portoflosangeles.org/business/statistics/facts-and-figures\">data from the Port of Los Angeles.</a> Supplies of these materials could be heavily depleted in the US due to the backlog of ships.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-small-businesses-gain-market-share-handle-supply-chain-disruptions-2021-3\">The Suez Canal won&#39;t be the last supply chain fail. Here are 4 things your small business can do to benefit from the next one.</a></em></p><p>Louttit said increases in consumer spending and, as a result, a spike in imports have overwhelmed the ports.</p><p>&#34;The ports are setting records moving cargo,&#34; Louttit told The Journal.</p><h2>California port delays are already helping drive shortages and delivery delays in the US</h2><p>California port delays seemed to have peaked in early February, but have persisted in recent months. </p><p>On January 30, Southern California port congestion <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/southern-california-ports-hit-record-level-of-ship-congestion-2021-1\">hit a record high when 38 container ships</a> were waiting along the coast for room to open up to dock and unload. </p><p>Gene Seroka, a Port of Los Angeles Executive, <a href=\"https://www.supplychaindive.com/news/california-port-congestion-los-angeles-long-beach-data/594715/\">warned</a> the Los Angeles Board of Harbor Commissioners in February that high import levels caused by increased spending during the pandemic were driving port congestion.</p><p>A video from the US Coast Guard shows dozens of ships anchored off the coast.</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/GnXAtM-7uv0\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe><p> </p><h2>California port delays are just one of many factors piling onto a global supply-chain crisis</h2><p>The boats waiting outside of the port, which can carry tens of thousands of shipping containers, are adding to the global container shortage, and, as a result, shipping delays.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/boat-stuck-suez-canal-latest-setback-global-supply-chain-crisis-2021-3\">Customers are already seeing the impact of shipping delays.</a> During a third-quarter earnings call in February, La-Z-Boy executives said customers should <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2021/03/08/furniture-sales-pandemic/\">expect delivery dates that are five to nine months out</a> from the purchase date.</p><p>The Texas freeze, as well as a shortage of computer chips, have already pushed companies to increase prices and delay production. Several companies including <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/boat-stuck-suez-canal-latest-setback-global-supply-chain-crisis-2021-3\">Nike, Honda, and Samsung have already said they have been hampered by supply-chain issues.</a></p><p>As a result of California port delays and the global container shortage, customers will likely face rising prices and limited options as commodities become increasingly difficult to obtain and produce, and companies are forced to compete for containers and delivery dates.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/603e771513b221001876b1f0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Compass Co-Founder and CEO, Robert Reffkin\" height=\"789\" width=\"1053\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Compass Co-Founder and Compass\n<p class=\"copyright\">Compass</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Robert Reffkin grew up in Berkeley, CA, with his mom, who is now a Compass agent.</li>\n<li>After graduating in two years from Columbia, he began his career on Wall Street. </li>\n<li>Reffkin took Compass public Thursday, making him one of just 8 Black billionaires in the US.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Robert Reffkin may soon be the youngest Black billionaire in the US after taking his real-estate startup Compass public on Thursday. </p><p>The 41-year-old cofounder and CEO has risen to prominence quickly. From growing up in Berkeley, CA with a single mom, to becoming a White House fellow and rising through the ranks at Goldman Sachs before launching Compass, here are some things to know about the up-and-coming executive.</p><h1>The women in his life have inspired him</h1><p>Reffkin grew up in Berkeley, CA, as an only child with a single mom, who is now a real estate agent for Compass. In a LinkedIn post Thursday after his company went public on the New York Stock Exchange, Reffkin said, &#34;I started Compass because of my mom, Ruth, a single mom who embodies the entrepreneurial spirit.&#34;</p><p>Today, Reffkin lives in New York City with his wife, Benis Reffkin, who is a <a href=\"https://www.benisreffkincoaching.com/\">business and life coach</a>. He dubbed her the &#34;<a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/most-important-person-my-life-robert-reffkin/\">most important person</a>&#34; in his life and an inspiration, in a LinkedIn post from Mother&#39;s Day 2019 that documented how she lived the American Dream. The couple have three kids together. </p><h1>He&#39;s been a founder before</h1><p>Reffkin started his first business when he was just 15 years old, according to an <a href=\"https://www.college.columbia.edu/cct/issue/summer17/article/%E2%80%9C-journey-was-exciting-part%E2%80%9D\">article from Columbia College Today</a>. Backed by babysitting and bar mitzvah money, the young founder started a DJ company called &#34;Rude Boy Productions&#34; that brought in a total of $100,000 by the time he graduated from high school, the article said. </p><p>In later years, Reffkin founded two philanthropic educational groups prior to starting Compass. One is Success Academy Charter Schools, a school system for low-income Black and Hispanic students in New York City that helps diminish educational disparities.</p><p>The second is a 501c3 non-profit called America Needs You, which according to its website, &#34;fights for economic mobility for ambitious, first-generation college students.&#34;</p><h1>He&#39;s a runner, too</h1><p>Though he founded two philanthropic organizations, Reffkin&#39;s generosity doesn&#39;t end there. Even his running hobby is helping others.</p><p>His &#34;primary philanthropic undertaking&#34; has been running a marathon in each of the 50 states in the US to raise $1 million for youth education and enrichment programs, he said in a <a href=\"https://www.americaneedsyou.org/team/profile/robert-reffkin/\">bio on America Needs You</a>. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60538d38f75f09001814eaae?format=jpeg\" alt=\"robert reffkin central park\" height=\"2982\" width=\"3988\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Reffkin running in Central Park in 2014.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Benjamin Lowy/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/compass-ipo-s1-profit-loss-real-estate-tech-brokerage-2021-3\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Compass is gearing up for an ambitious $10 billion IPO. We pored over its 261-page S-1 filing and came away with 5 key revelations.</a></em></p><h1>He rose through the ranks on Wall Street</h1><p>Reffkin graduated from Columbia University in just under two years, according to Fortune, which placed him on the 40 under 40 list in 2014. He then became the youngest business analyst ever hired at McKinsey &#38; Company where he spent two years before returning to his alma mater to get his MBA and then going back to Wall Street as an associate at Lazard. </p><p>He then rose through the ranks at Goldman Sachs, eventually becoming the chief of staff for Gary Cohn, the former president and chief operating officer of Goldman. But he left the storied Wall Street firm in 2012 to start his company. </p><h1>Real estate isn&#39;t his forte</h1><p>Reffkin left his banking career to start up Compass with the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/compass-technical-cofounder-ori-allon-2021-3\">tech entrepreneur Ori Allon</a>. But <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/robert-reffkin-compass-ceo-ipo-real-estate-brokerage-goldman-sachs-2021-3\">sources told Insider previously</a> he didn&#39;t actually know much about the industry he was trying to disrupt, saying he had a rudimentary knowledge and didn&#39;t know the difference between a co-op and an apartment. </p><p>Doing things he&#39;s uncomfortable with is just part of his personality, though. One person said he&#39;s lacked experience in almost everything he&#39;s ever done but that&#39;s part of what makes him an &#34;extraordinary person.&#34;</p><p>His former boss, Cohn, said Reffkin just has an &#34;aura of confidence.&#34;</p><h1>He may someday run for public office</h1><p>In 2005, he was <a href=\"https://georgewbush-whitehouse.archives.gov/fellows/alumni/2005-06.html\">a White House fellow</a> under the George W. Bush administration, where he served as the special assistant to the Secretary of the Treasury, John Snow.</p><p>He&#39;s always had big ambitions for his career, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/robert-reffkin-compass-ceo-ipo-real-estate-brokerage-goldman-sachs-2021-3\">sources told Insider previously</a>. Those close to him have said he has talked about someday running for public office, such as mayor of New York City. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Sery Kim, a candidate running for the 6th congressional district in Texas, has lost two GOP endorsements after news that she made anti-Asian remarks. </p><p>In early March, Sery Kim, who is <a href=\"https://seryfortexas.com/about/\">Korean American</a>, received the backing of California Republican Reps. Young Kim and Michelle Steel. The two have since dropped their endorsement, following Sery Kim&#39;s comments earlier this week, in which she said Chinese immigrants aren&#39;t welcome in the US.</p><p>During a <a href=\"https://www.eventbrite.com/e/arcrwa-cd-6-republican-candidate-forum-tickets-145134748941#\">GOP candidate forum</a> on Wednesday, Sery Kim and others running talked about China&#39;s influence and immigrants who come to the US from China.</p><p>&#34;I don&#39;t want them here at all,&#34; Sery Kim said about Chinese immigrants, to applause from the audience. &#34;They steal our intellectual property. They give us coronavirus. They don&#39;t hold themselves accountable.&#34;</p><p>&#34;Quite frankly, I can say that because I&#39;m Korean.&#34;</p><p>In a <a href=\"https://thehill.com/homenews/campaign/546329-gop-reps-kim-steel-pull-endorsement-of-congressional-candidate-following?rl=1\">statement</a>, the two California lawmakers said they &#34;cannot in good conscience&#34; continue to back Sery Kim. </p><p>&#34;As the first Korean American Republican women to serve in Congress, we want to empower and lift up fellow members of the AAPI [Asian American and Pacific Island] community who want to serve their communities,&#34; the lawmakers wrote. </p><p>They asked Sery Kim to apologize for her remarks, saying they &#34;talked with Sery Kim yesterday about her hurtful and untrue comments about Chinese immigrants, and made clear that her comments were unacceptable.&#34;</p><p>Sery Kim has not &#34;publicly shown remorse, and her words were contrary to what we stand for,&#34; they said, also adding that the two &#34;will continue to speak out in support of our AAPI community.&#34;</p><p>Sery Kim, speaking to CNN, said her remarks were intended only with respect to the Chinese Communist Party.</p><p>&#34;I am shocked that in an effort to counter Asian-American hate the liberal media is targeting me, an Asian and an immigrant, in an effort to paint me as anti-Asian and anti-immigrant just for speaking against the oppressive Chinese Communist Party,&#34; Sery Kim said in a statement to <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/04/02/politics/sery-kim-endorsement-texas-candidate-chinese-immigrants/index.html\">CNN</a>. She did not immediately return Insider&#39;s request for comment.</p><p>Sery Kim&#39;s comments come at the same time as numerous anti-Asian attacks unfold.</p><p>Just on Monday, a 65-year-old Asian woman was <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/elderly-asian-woman-assaulted-new-york-city-in-broad-daylight-2021-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"ac76b2eda12f87f96542e6d8f5ce0fff\">assaulted and yelled at in broad daylight on a New York City sidewalk</a>. Her assailant, <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/man-arrested-over-attack-65-year-old-asian-woman-nypd-2021-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"201db4c773daf4bc6e61c2955e1e5aaf\">38-year-old Brandon Elliot</a>, kicked her to the ground and stomped on her head repeatedly while two doormen in a luxury apartment watched, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/NYPDTips/status/1376725286167924741\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"683db15913e921b219b1f1ae2dc24ed4\">security footage</a> released by the police shows. When Elliot walked away, the doormen closed the apartment doors on her. </p><p>Nationally, recent stories related to anti-Asian violence also paint a grim picture.</p><p>Two weeks ago, police arrested a man in connection to a string of <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/deadly-spa-shootings-in-atlanta-metro-area-2021-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"612022ec9a9d514b7fb5562f26433199\">deadly shootings at three Atlanta-area massage parlors</a>. Six out of eight of the victims were Asian women. Each attack had taken place at three massage parlors within an hour of one another on Tuesday.</p><p>The shooter, 21-year-old <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/robert-aaron-long-atlanta-spa-shooting-suspect-2021-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"5298e2657f648fc9348364e07c4df8c1\">Robert Aaron Long</a> from Woodstock, Georgia, suggested to police that the attacks were due to a sex addiction and were not racially motivated.</p><p>Sery Kim is running to take the seat left open by the deceased Rep. Ron Wright. She had previously worked in the Small Business Administration in the era of former President Donald Trump.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"Johnson & Johnson takes over COVID-19 vaccine production at Baltimore plant after 15 million doses were ruined","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/johnson-johnson-runs-covid-19-vaccine-production-baltimore-removes-astrazeneca-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/601575776dfbe10018e00ecc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"johnson and johnson covid vaccine\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Johnson &#38; Johnson&#39;s coronavirus vaccine is delivered as a single shot, while both Pfizer and Moderna&#39;s require two jabs.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thiago PrudÃªncio/SOPA Images/LightRocket via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Johnson &#38; Johnson has been put in charge of COVID-19 vaccine production at a Baltimore plant.</li>\n<li>The move comes after 15 million COVID-19 vaccine doses were ruined in a mixup.</li>\n<li>The error did not impact any vaccines that are currently being delivered or used.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Johnson &#38; Johnson, with the aid of President Joe Biden&#39;s administration, has been put in charge of a Baltimore vaccine production plant <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/factory-mixup-ruins-johnson-johnson-doses-nyt-2021-3\">that ruined 15 million doses</a> of its COVID-19 vaccine and has moved to stop British drugmaker AstraZeneca Plc from utilizing the facility to avoid any future mistakes, senior federal health officials said on Saturday.</p><p>The extraordinary decision, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/live/2021/04/03/world/covid-vaccine-coronavirus-cases/the-biden-administration-puts-johnson-johnson-in-charge-of-a-baltimore-plant-that-ruined-millions-of-doses-of-its-vaccine\">which was first reported by The New York Times</a>, was put into action by the US Department of Health and Human Services and will allow the Emergent BioSolutions plant to focus on making the single-dose Johnson &#38; Johnson COVID-19 vaccine.</p><p>Johnson &#38; Johnson confirmed the move on Saturday, stating that it was &#34;assuming full responsibility regarding the manufacturing of drug substance&#34; at Emergent.</p><p>&#34;Specifically, the company is adding dedicated leaders for operations and quality, and significantly increasing the number of manufacturing, quality and technical operations personnel to work with the company specialists already at Emergent,&#34; Johnson &#38; Johnson said in a statement.</p><p>The change comes after the disclosure that Emergent, which is a manufacturing partner to both AstraZeneca and Johnson &#38; Johnson, mixed up ingredients from the two coronavirus vaccines in a case of human error, causing regulators to delay authorization of the facility&#39;s vaccine production.</p><p>The mixup ruined nearly 15 million Johnson &#38; Johnson doses.</p><p>The error did not impact any vaccines that are currently being delivered or used, according to the Times report.</p><p><strong><em>Read more: </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/issues-that-could-tank-bidens-infrastructure-plan-congress-salt-taxes-2021-4\"><em>Here are 9 hurdles Biden&#39;s infrastructure plan would have to overcome in Congress before it can become law</em></a></p><p>The Biden administration has made note of the delay and has not shifted <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-us-will-have-vaccines-300-million-people-may-2021-3\">its stated goal</a> of having enough vaccines for all adult Americans by the end of May.</p><p>According to the Times report, federal officials are concerned that the mixup could dampen confidence in the vaccines just as Biden <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-demands-governors-reinstate-mask-mandates-covid-19-cases-rise-2021-3\">is aggressively pushing</a> for mask mandates to remain in place as new COVID-19 variants spread throughout the US.</p><p>Meanwhile, <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/uk-astrazeneca-covid19-vaccine-safe-despite-rising-blood-clot-cases-2021-4\">there are concerns</a> about the two-dose AstraZeneca vaccine, which has had a troubled rollout in Europe due to a risk of rare blood clots <a href=\"https://www.ema.europa.eu/en/news/covid-19-vaccine-astrazeneca-benefits-still-outweigh-risks-despite-possible-link-rare-blood-clots\">possibly linked</a> to the vaccine. However, the United Kingdom&#39;s drug regulator deemed the vaccine as safe.</p><p>AstraZeneca said that it would work with the Biden administration to find an alternative site for its vaccine production, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-us-hasnt-authorized-astrazeneca-shot-when-that-may-change-2021-3\">which has not yet been authorized</a> in the US.</p><p data-el=\"text\">&#34;AstraZeneca and the US government continue to work closely together to support agreed upon plans for the development, production and full delivery of the vaccine,&#34; the company wrote in a statement.</p><p>With three vaccines authorized in the US - from Johnson &#38; Johnson, Pfizer-BioNTech, and Moderna - it is unclear if there will even be a need for an additional vaccine.</p><p>Dr. Anthony Fauci, the nation&#39;s top infectious-disease expert, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-astrazeneca-exclus/exclusive-fauci-says-u-s-may-not-need-astrazeneca-covid-19-vaccine-idUSKBN2BO6XS\">said as much</a> in a recent interview with Reuters.</p><p>&#34;That&#39;s still up in the air,&#34; Fauci said. &#34;My general feeling is that given the contractual relationships that we have with a number of companies, that we have enough vaccine to fulfill all of our needs without invoking AstraZeneca.&#34;</p><p>However, a federal official said that the HHS is in talks with AstraZeneca &#34;to adapt its vaccine to combat new coronavirus variants,&#34; according to the Times report.</p><p>As of Sunday, nearly 30.7 million Americans have tested positive for the coronavirus and more than 554,000 people have died of the illness, based on data compiled by <a href=\"https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"d5d56d2c446e664e73dc4acddf377455\">Johns Hopkins University</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Dorman)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/601575776dfbe10018e00ecc?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn14@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-45-41-398_6164b4a62a255df0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn6@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-09-303_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=gDfg4BBf8fk:W9gyZ41SLcg:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn26@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-09-428_93c70569a9be45b0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=gDfg4BBf8fk:W9gyZ41SLcg:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn23@2020_2/2021/04/05/06-46-03-392_d3109438a051a021.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-06-748_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=gDfg4BBf8fk:W9gyZ41SLcg:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn9@2020_2/2021/04/05/06-46-10-586_ee5797d922faf5f7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/gDfg4BBf8fk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn88@2020_5/2021/04/05/06-46-11-055_50e0f530645e1333.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617605114833},{"createdTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"3 creators and a lawyer share how social media bans work, and the best way to safeguard your account","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-avoid-banned-social-media-creators-lawyer-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60649974daf0f10018f993ba?format=jpeg\" alt=\"fitness influencer\" height=\"2673\" width=\"3564\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Accidentally playing copyrighted music in the background of your video can put your account at risk.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty/Ivan Pantic</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>When influencers or creators are banned for known or unknown reasons, it can impact their income.</li>\n<li>Three creators and a lawyer shared their experiences with social media bans.</li>\n<li>They advised avoiding using third-party content and being cautious while livestreaming. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Getting banned on social media isn&#39;t just a nuisance for influencers and creators. Oftentimes these platforms are a huge part of their livelihood - and the longer they&#39;re unable to create content and share it with their audience, the more money they lose out on.</p><p>Bans are often instituted by a platform for reasons including harassment, bullying, or copyright or policy violations, but they can also happen for unknown reasons or by accident. </p><p>They&#39;re also surprisingly common: Twitter suspended <a href=\"https://www.wired.com/story/opinion-social-media-bans-are-really-actually-shockingly-common/\">roughly 925,000 accounts</a> during the first half of 2020 alone, and, in June 2019, Instagram conducted a &#34;<a href=\"https://www.insider.com/instagram-meme-page-purge-suspends-accounts-2019-7\">meme page purge</a>,&#34; removing accounts with a combined reach of 30 million followers. Those pages&#39; creators lost out on tens of thousands of dollars in placements, sponsorships, and advertising income. </p><p>Three creators and a lawyer shared how to avoid getting removed from a platform.</p><h2>Know the risks of using third-party materials</h2><p>A 30-year-old influencer who goes by the name Produced By Blanco has been making music professionally since 2018. He&#39;s worked with artists signed to major labels including Atlantic, Roc Nation, Sony, Columbia, Republic, and Universal, has 12,500 followers on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/producedbyblanco/\">Instagram</a>, and has <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yi90p-4yk74\">driven millions of views on YouTube</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606494256183e10019819805?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Â© Produced By Blanco\" height=\"539\" width=\"719\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Produced By Blanco.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Produced By Blanco</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Blanco told Insider he avoids terms-of-use violations, like sharing unauthorized content, by only sharing his own content or content made by artists he&#39;s worked with. </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s the safest route,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.lauritsenesq.com/\">Eric Lauritsen</a>, a Los Angeles-based music industry attorney who&#39;s represented clients who&#39;ve been banned from platforms like Twitch and TikTok, told Insider. But creators don&#39;t have to follow Blanco&#39;s all-or-nothing approach as long as they understand the risks. </p><p>&#34;To be safe, make it a policy not to use material owned by third parties,&#34; he said. &#34;But, if you intend to use third-party material anyway, you may be OK doing it, but at a minimum, accept the fact that a third-party will <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/6013276?hl=en\">claim the revenue</a> or your content is at risk of removal. Some parties may go further though and may want to pursue a claim against you for statutory damages,&#34; he added, citing the landmark <a href=\"https://scholar.google.com/scholar_case?case=11742536547701554911&q=metallica+lawsuit&hl=en&as_sdt=2,23;as_sdt=2,23\">Napster</a> case in 2000, where Metallica sued for $100,000 in damages per song illegally downloaded on the site. </p><p>Most social media platforms treat the use of copyrighted material the same, whether it&#39;s by accident (for example, someone else&#39;s song playing in the background of your livestream) or on purpose (like blatantly stealing it). And saying &#34;no copyright infringement&#34; won&#39;t protect you, either.</p><h2>Control as much of your content as possible</h2><p>Matthew Pettito, 18, has 3.8 million followers on <a href=\"https://vm.tiktok.com/ZMeN3WQQ9/\">TikTok</a>, 192,000 followers on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/mattpetitto/?hl=en\">Instagram</a>, 26,000 followers on <a href=\"https://www.twitch.tv/mattpetitto\">Twitch</a>, and is sponsored by energy-drink company <a href=\"https://bangenergy.com/\">Bang Energy</a>. He first downloaded TikTok in July 2019 and said he had one million followers by June 2020. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6064947d6183e10019819808?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Â© Matthew Petitto\" height=\"540\" width=\"720\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Matthew Petitto.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Matthew Petitto</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>He began livestreaming on TikTok to start making money through the <a href=\"https://newsroom.tiktok.com/en-us/introducing-the-200-million-tiktok-creator-fund\">TikTok Creator Program</a> (per the Creator terms, you need at least 1,000 followers to be eligible to monetize your livestream). While hosting a TikTok livestream one night, Pettito was also on Omegle, a free app that facilitates chats with strangers online.  </p><p>&#34;There are no community guidelines, so it&#39;s not uncommon for people on the website to be saying or doing vulgar things,&#34; Pettito told Insider. &#34;I was on track to make $1,000 that night, and all of a sudden, I was removed from the app and banned for 48 hours.&#34; He lost the $1,000 due to the vulgar comment being picked up on his livestream.</p><p>Pettito recommended other influencers use caution while streaming live &#34;because you can&#39;t edit or take back anything,&#34; he said. Some users even record livestream content and upload it to other platforms, so whatever you say or do can take on a life of its own - for better or worse.</p><h2>Consider hiring an attorney if you have a significant amount of money at stake</h2><p>Dakota Elder, 27, had his YouTube account banned in 2019 and his TikTok account banned in 2020. At the time, he said he had 100,000 subscribers on YouTube and 500,000 followers on TikTok. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606494d6daf0f10018f9938f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Â© Dakota Elder\" height=\"810\" width=\"1080\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dakota Elder.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dakota Elder</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>He told Insider he still doesn&#39;t know why either account was banned and didn&#39;t hear back from either platform when he asked why. Elder was on track to make about $2,500 in revenue the following month from both accounts.</p><p>&#34;There&#39;s going to be a lot of variation depending on the terms of use of the site and the user&#39;s activity before the ban,&#34; Lauritsen said about why platforms may not reveal the reason behind the ban. &#34;The site may not even be obligated to provide a reason.&#34;</p><p>Elder now has over 4.4 million followers on his new <a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@dakota.e?\">TikTok</a> profile but chose not to recreate his YouTube channel. Despite being permanently banned from both, he created the new TikTok account by just signing up again. </p><p>&#34;Making the new account was smooth as butter,&#34; he said. &#34;I had no problems, and I haven&#39;t had an issue since the first video on the new account.&#34; It was easy to sign back up again, he said, although he couldn&#39;t access the old account, followers, or content. </p><p>Taking the revenue hit was likely the most cost-effective option for Elder, but for creators with a significant amount of money at stake, consulting an attorney could be worth it. </p><p>&#34;I have seen scenarios where clients had music taken down from streaming services, reached out, did not receive a response, then hired me to follow up and I was able to get information,&#34; Lauritsen said. &#34;There is an extra air of legitimacy using an attorney to at least help get you more information.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-avoid-banned-social-media-creators-lawyer-2021-4'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:V_sGLiPBpWU\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:gIN9vFwOqvQ\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/biUvEZA2Noo\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 04 Apr 2021 13:15:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/60649a2c6183e1001981983c?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"ae3800a0bacc61c5e365281547f64950","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn70@2020_2/2021/04/05/06-46-02-963_1c580382af744736.webp","destWidth":720,"destHeight":540,"sourceBytes":20904,"destBytes":20904,"author":"insider@insider.com (Brian J. Roberts)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60649974daf0f10018f993ba?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn84@2020_1/2021/04/05/06-46-04-370_f0075c94f8a85d06.webp","https://i.insider.com/606494256183e10019819805?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn46@2020_5/2021/04/05/06-46-06-436_07c7b462ffaaf8d1.webp","https://i.insider.com/6064947d6183e10019819808?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn9@2020_4/2021/04/05/06-46-08-139_dafbac0a359af673.webp","https://i.insider.com/606494d6daf0f10018f9938f?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn10@2020_1/2021/04/05/06-46-08-549_f273eb9022fded3f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn6@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-09-303_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn16@2020_6/2021/04/05/06-46-04-994_cc534042dcd12ece.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn41@2020_1/2021/04/05/06-46-08-453_00763513e3ddb13d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn97@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-06-748_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=biUvEZA2Noo:9wBB-xGplw8:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn93@2020_1/2021/04/05/06-46-06-696_19701e0a5b29fdcd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/biUvEZA2Noo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn73@2020_3/2021/04/05/06-46-05-648_c47972a39e4f74d7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617605114847},{"createdTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","updatedTime":"2021-04-05 14:45:14","title":"Democrats can learn something from the most powerful Joe in Washington","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/democrats-learn-something-joe-manchin-most-powerful-joe-washington-dc-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606725f7902281001950abca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Joe Manchin 2\" height=\"957\" width=\"1914\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sen. Joe Manchin.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo By Tom Williams/CQ-Roll Call, Inc via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Sen. Joe Manchin is the deciding vote in the Senate, making him the most powerful Joe in Washington.</li>\n<li>While his moderate policies frustrate some Democrats, he also has an important lesson to teach them.</li>\n<li>He wins in a deep red state and if more Democrats could win elections like him, then his moderate stances wouldn&#39;t be as much of an issue.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>President Joe Biden is the first Joe in the White House, ever. But even though he&#39;s Commander-in-Chief, there&#39;s another politician named Joe who may have more power than our president: West Virginia Sen. Joe Manchin.</p><h2><strong>The most powerful Joe in Washington</strong></h2><p>Joe Biden has the big ideas - infrastructure, voting rights, racial healing, jobs, guns, climate, and, of course, nailing COVID- but as we learned with the stimulus bill, Joe Manchin has the final say on what gets passed. <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2021/3/6/22313466/covid-stimulus-package-passes-unemployment\">Manchin&#39;s opposition</a> ultimately doomed the $15 minimum wage, reduced eligibility for stimulus checks, and forced last-minute tweaks to unemployment insurance expansion.</p><p>And when Manchin said he&#39;d vote against Neera Tanden, Biden&#39;s original nominee to lead the Office of Management and Budget, her fate was all but sealed in a Senate split 50 Democrats to 50 Republicans.</p><p>Everyone&#39;s waiting with baited breath every time Manchin speaks - what does he think about the filibuster? When he said he&#39;s open to <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/07/us/politics/joe-manchin-filibuster-stimulus.html\">making the filibuster harder</a>, Democrats were aglow that they could pass more of Biden&#39;s ambitious agenda.</p><p>What kind of gun safety does he support? He has publicly come out <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/23/politics/manchin-house-gun-bills-democrats/index.html\">against the two gun safety bills</a> passed by the House in March that expand background checks for most gun purchases, instead preferring background checks only for commercial gun transactions.</p><p>Where does he stand on voting rights? Manchin is the only Democrat who is<a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/joe-manchin-faces-home-state-pressure-to-oppose-democrats-voting-bill-11616518816\"> not co-sponsoring</a> the For the People Act legislation in the Senate and is<a href=\"https://nymag.com/intelligencer/2021/03/manchin-values-bipartisanship-over-voting-rights.html\"> pushing for bipartisan compromise</a>.</p><p>Joe Manchin is at the exact center point of the Senate ideologically and therefore numerically. He represents among the reddest of red states, which gave loser President Donald Trump 68% of the vote, even in 2020. So Manchin stays alive by tacking towards the center, not the left.</p><h2><strong>The most narrow majority possible</strong></h2><p>Manchin being the focal point has frustrated those of us who want Biden to make real progress on his agenda. The president needed a Democratic Senate to get anything of note done, and the wise people of Georgia provided that. Now the expectations could not be higher.</p><p>Every time Joe Manchin peeks to his right a bit, there&#39;s speculation that he&#39;ll <a href=\"https://www.realclearpolitics.com/video/2021/01/11/manchin_on_changing_parties_im_a_good_old_west_virginia_conservative_democrat.html\">switch parties</a> - which <a href=\"https://www.wsaz.com/content/news/Senator-Manchin-refutes-speculation-of-a-party-switch--400628491.html\">Manchin flatly dismisses</a> - or <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2021/02/02/manchin-sinema-challengers-464821\">be challenged in a primary</a>.</p><p>But we need every Democrat we can get to maintain a majority. The moderates give the Dems the majority in the House and Senate. And if the party starts to lose purple states and swing districts, it will lose the majority.</p><p>The Democrats, of course, should have a bigger majority in the Senate. They lost a bunch of winnable races in 2018 and 2020 - such as Cal Cunningham in North Carolina, who lost after a sexting scandal. If more purple or even deep red state Dems were able to get elected like Manchin, his vote and the margin wouldn&#39;t be as much of an issue. So Manchin is invaluable in the sense that he can actually win in a place that no other Dem would really have a chance, and he can win when Dems in other, seemingly more friendly states, cannot.</p><p>In the meantime, let&#39;s live with Manchin, because if he switched parties Mitch McConnell would be leader. If he lost in a primary, West Virginians would elect a Republican. We need Joe Manchin right now because if we lost him, we also would lose any chance at progress.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a pandemic","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/godzilla-vs-kong-opens-to-best-box-office-during-pandemic-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6069d22aa7d803001963ea8c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"godzilla vs kong\" height=\"1176\" width=\"2392\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;Godzilla vs. Kong&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Warner Bros.</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>&#34;Godzilla vs. Kong&#34; earned $48.5 million in its five-day opening weekend at the US box office.</li>\n<li>It&#39;s the best opening yet for a movie at the domestic box office during the year-long pandemic.</li>\n<li>It signals hope for movie theaters, though the industry still has a long road to recovery.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>&#34;Godzilla vs. Kong&#34; beat the odds over the weekend at the box office.</p><p>The new monster movie from Warner Bros. <a href=\"https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/box-office-godzilla-vs-kong-defeats-pandemic-with-48m-u-s-start?utm_source=twitter&utm_medium=socialcial\">earned $48.5 million</a> at the US box office in its first five days (it opened in theaters on Wednesday), and $32.2 million over the three-day Easter weekend from 3,064 theaters.</p><p>It&#39;s the best domestic opening yet for a movie during the coronavirus pandemic, which has devastated the theatrical industry over the past year. The movie grossed $121 million during its international opening last month, which was also a pandemic-best. Its <a href=\"https://deadline.com/2021/04/godzilla-vs-kong-second-weekend-china-global-international-box-office-1234727363/\">global total</a> is now $285 million.</p><p>The movie&#39;s predecessor, &#34;Godzilla: King of the Monsters,&#34; earned $47.8 million domestically over its first three-day weekend in 2019. It went on to earn $110.5 million domestically and $386 million worldwide.</p><p>It&#39;s more impressive considering that &#34;Godzilla vs. Kong&#34; debuted on WarnerMedia&#39;s streaming service HBO Max for no additional fee to subscribers on the same day it hit theaters in the US, as are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/warner-bros-movie-2021-debut-hbo-max-theaters-same-day-2020-12\">all of Warner Bros.&#39; movies this year</a>.</p><p>Theaters across the country are also operating at limited capacity, including in New York City, one of the biggest theatrical markets in the US that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/new-york-city-movie-theaters-to-reopen-2021-2\">finally opened last month</a> after a year of being shut down.</p><p>While the numbers would normally be underwhelming for a blockbuster that cost $200 million to produce, &#34;Godzilla vs. Kong&#39;s&#34; strong start signals hope for movie theaters - though they <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-comfortable-americans-feel-returning-to-movie-theaters-survey-2021-3\">still have a long road to full recovery</a>.</p><p>The last pandemic-best domestic opening was Warner Bros.&#39; &#34;Wonder Woman 1984&#34; in December <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/wonder-woman-1984-opens-with-best-box-office-during-pandemic-2020-12\">with $16.7 million</a>. The movie also debuted on HBO Max simultaneously with theaters. While it would ultimately slow at the box office with a $45 million domestic total (and $165 million worldwide), data showed that it <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/wonder-woman-1984-helping-hbo-max-slow-box-office-data-2021-1\">boosted HBO Max signups</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
